Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 966/2012 on the codification of Regulation (EC) No 1365/2006
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?

KEY POINTS

transport of goods, goods not in containers and empty containers, goods transported in the course of household and office removals, baggage transported separately from passengers, motor vehicles being moved for repair, and other non-market goods;

number of movements of loaded vessels and movements of empty vessels;
movements of vessels (loaded vessels)

The European Statistical System Committee (ESSC) is responsible for monitoring the implementation of the regulation. It is chaired by the European Commission and comprises representatives of the EU countries and Eurostat.
The Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 10 concerning the amendment of this regulation in order to raise the threshold for inland waterways data collection to take account of economic and technical trends. These delegated acts must be adopted by 31 December 2020 and every 5 years thereafter.

Eurostat must submit a report to the European Parliament and to the Council on the implementation and on future developments.

Summary 49:
Visa-free travel with non-EU countries: the Schengen reciprocity mechanism
Visa - visa - visa exemption
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1931/2006 on the visa exemption mechanism
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EU) No 1/2002/EC, which originally applied to non-European Union (EU)* countries whose nationals are exempt from the visa requirement.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
non-EU nationals who do not hold the nationality of any EU country, who reside in an EU Member State and who are holders of a travel document issued by that Member State;
nationals of new third countries formerly part of and stateless persons and other persons who are not nationals of any country, but who do reside in a Member State, and who have the travel document of an EU country;
travel documents and visas issued by the Member State.
The exemption applies to all the nationals of the Member States concerned, except those who are nationals of:
the United Kingdom of Great Britain and Northern Ireland;
the Republic of Ireland; and
the People’s Republic of China.
Exemption from visa requirement
The Member State concerned must notify the European Commission of the date and type of travel document and visa it intends to issue and the types of travel documents it plans to issue. The notification must include a detailed explanation of the preliminary measures it has taken with a view to ensuring that the visa is issued and all relevant information.
the date of implementation of the visa and the nature of the travel documents and visa.
If the Commission considers it necessary, it may suspend the exemption for a period of 6 months. If the Commission has submitted a legislative proposal, the period of suspension of the exemption is extended by six months.
Implementing acts
The implementing acts must be adopted by the European Parliament and the Council in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 11(2) of the regulation. The Commission must adopt implementing acts within 6 months of receiving the Commission's proposal.
In addition, the Commission must submit an implementing act to the Council and the Parliament every 3 years. This must contain:
a description of the type and nature of visa and travel document;
a list of the countries covered by the regulation;
an explanation of preliminary measures that the EU country concerned has taken in order to ensure visa-free visa travel with the third country in question;
all relevant information relating to the type, nature and duration of the non-visa and travel documents issued and the validity of those travel documents;
any measures taken by the Commission to ensure the visa-issuing Member State to ensure that its nationals are not subject to a visa requirement;
procedures for the exchange of information between the Commission and the third countries concerned.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 6 November 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
The European Union has adopted a number of measures to improve the visa system, including:
reciprocal travel arrangements between Member States and non-member countries;
visa liberalisation agreements between the European Union and its Member States;
recovery mechanisms for non-Member States and third countries.
For more information, see:
‘Visa liberalisation’ on the website of the European External Action Service (EEAS).
KEY TERMS
* Non-EU country: a non-governmental organisation (NGO) or any other institution, body, office or agency of the Union or international organisation competent in matters covered by this regulation.
* Travel document: any travel document or visa issued by an EU member state.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еганка народна года барка, горадка  галка (OJ L 131, 1.6.2018, pp. 1-3)
Successive amendments to the regulation have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 50:
Eurojust’s legal framework — rules on the protection of privacy and fundamental rights and freedoms of individuals (Regulation (EU) No 1304/2014)
Eurojust's legal framework – rules on privacy and respect for the rights of individuals
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation No 1303/2014/EU on the legal framework of Eurojust
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules on Eurojust, a European Union (EU)-wide network of law enforcement and judicial bodies.
It sets out Eurojust's rules on:
the functions of the national members, the College and the Administrative Director;
the College's functions and responsibilities; and
the role of the Executive Board.
KEY POINTS
   
The regulation sets out the rules governing Eurojust‘s legal structure:
EuroJust’ is governed by a College of national members (known as Eurojust College) and an Executive Board (Eurojust Executive Board). It is chaired by the European Parliament, the Council and the European Police Organisation (EPPO). The College meets at least once a month. The Executive Board is composed of representatives of the EU countries’ national members and the EPPO.
The College is responsible for:
monitoring and evaluating Eurojust;
assisting Eurojust in its work;
ensuring that Eurojust complies with the rules of the European Criminal Police Office (Interpol); and
keeping a record of operational personal data.
In the event of a personal data breach, Eurojust must notify the competent authorities of the Member States concerned. It may also order, request or execute any request for mutual legal assistance or mutual recognition, as provided for in Directive 2014/41/EU.
Annex I of the regulation lists the categories of categories of processing activities Eurojust may undertake, including:
operational personal data relating to the circumstances of an offence, where such data are immediately relevant to and are included in ongoing investigations which Eurojust is coordinating or helping to coordinate and when their processing is necessary for the purposes specified in the regulation;
processing of operational data related to the investigation;
processing operational data other than the personal data referred to in Annex II relating to:
criminal investigations;
investigations;
criminal proceedings;
prosecutions;
immunity of individuals;
protection of the privacy of individuals’ personal data;
protecting the right of individuals to have their personal data processed and stored in a secure manner;
respect for the right to privacy of persons’ data and of the fundamental rights of the individuals concerned.
EU countries may, in exceptional cases, temporarily store and analyse each new temporary work file that contains personal data, subject to the purpose limitation principle applicable to processing of personal data in the context of all its activities. The national member may decide by way of derogation to store those data until the following review. It must inform the European Commission of any such decision. The Commission must inform Eurojust of the reasons for this decision and inform the national authorities of any new temporary storage.
A European Parliament and Council Standing Committee on the Protection of the Rights and Freedoms of Persons’ Personal Data, which meets regularly at Eurojust headquarters, has the power to adopt appropriate provisions that apply to all Eurojust staff and members of their families. The committee may adopt measures to protect the rights and liberties of individuals and to ensure Eurojust operates in line with the principles of privacy, respect for human rights and fundamental freedoms. It also adopts measures to ensure the confidentiality of national proceedings and decisions.
Amendments to the regulation
In 2018, the regulation was amended in order to clarify the roles and responsibilities of the College, the executive board and the administrative director. The College is the decision-making body responsible for the management of the Eurojust network. It is assisted by an Executive Director, who is appointed by Eurojust on the basis of a proposal from Eurojust. The executive board meets at at least twice a month and meets at the request of each Member State. It has a number of members, including the Commission, the European Anti-Fraud Office (EPPO), the European Judicial Network and Eurojust Executive Director. It adopts the budget for the current financial year and the establishment plan for the following financial year. The European Union contribution and other subsidies chargeable to the general budget of the Union are not included in the budget. The budget must be approved by the Commission and the Council in accordance with the EU budgetary procedure.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATED APPLY?

It has applied since 1 July 2014.
BACKGROUND
 
Euro-just is a network of national law enforcement bodies and judicial authorities in the European Union. It was set up in 2013.
For more information, see:
About Eurojust (European External Action Service).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom)



Summary 51:
Criminal offences and sanctions in the area of money laundering: rules for natural persons and entities responsible for money laundering (Directive (EU) 2015/849)
Criminal sanctions and rules for legal persons involved in money laundering
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2014/40/EU on criminal offences and penalties in the field of money-laundering
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
   
 
It aims to combat money laundering by means of criminal law, enabling more efficient and swifter cross-border cooperation between EU countries’ competent authorities.
It establishes minimum rules concerning the definition of criminal offences, penalties and sanctions for persons who commit, or were involved in, the criminal activity from which the property was derived.
KEY POINTS
EU countries must ensure that the conduct referred to in points (a) and (b) of paragraph 1 is punishable as a criminal offence when committed by persons who are:
persons who committed, or who were involved, in criminal activities; or
natural persons acting as obliged entities in the exercise of their professional activities.
Penalties for individuals and entities are based on the following:
the offence was committed within the framework of a criminal organisation within the meaning of Framework Decision 2008/841/JHA;
the offender is an obliged entity, or has committed the offence in the course of professional activities;
an obliged entity is liable for the benefit of that legal person under its authority.
Legal persons can be held liable where the lack of supervision or control by a legal person has made possible the commission of any of the offences referred to above.
The European Commission must submit a report to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee on the implementation of this directive by 3 December 2022 assessing the extent to which EU countries have taken the necessary measures to comply with this directive.
In criminal proceedings regarding money laundering, EU countries should assist each other in the widest possible way and ensure that information is exchanged in an effective and timely manner in accordance with national law and the existing EU legal framework. The freezing and confiscation of instrumentalities and proceeds of crime remove the financial incentives which drive crime.
Reporting
The Commission will submit to the EU Parliament and to the Council a report on its implementation and assess the extent of the measures taken by EU countries. The Commission will take into account the information provided by Member States.

Summary 52:
Recovery of bluefin tuna in the eastern Atlantic and Mediterranean: Regulation (EU) No 552/2012
Recovering of bluefins
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU), Euratom — multiannual recovery plan for bluefin tunas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the recovery of blue fins (bluefin tuna) in the Eastern Atlantic and the Mediterranean.
It repeals Regulation (EC) No 302/2009.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
fishing vessels over 24 metres;
caging vessels;
recreational fishing vessels.
Fishing vessels must comply with the following rules:
capture the fish in cages or traps;
release the fish into the sea;
transfer the fish to a farm.
By-catch
EU countries must:
ensure that by-catch vessels comply with:
the rules on by-catching;
the procedures on the transfer of the fish from the cages to the farm;
recourse to the International Convention for the Conservation of Atlantic Tunas (ICCAT);
monitoring of the movements of tuna.
Caging operations
EU governments must ensure that: at least 15 days before the start of an operation, each EU country sends the information referred to in the regulation to the European Commission in the format set out in Annex VI. The Commission forwards the information to the ICCAT Secretariat.
The information must include: the number and weight of fish in each caging operation;the date and time and position of the transfer;the total number of fish caught and the total weight of the transferred fish;the number of caged fish and the number of transferred fish.
If the Commission receives a request for a transfer, it must inform the EU country responsible for the caging vessel, trap or, if applicable, farm within one working day following the request and the submission of the information.
Refusal of transfer authorisation
If an EU country considers that a transfer has not been carried out in accordance with the regulation’s rules, it may refuse to grant the authorisation.
Monitoring and reporting
EU fisheries authorities must ensure:
that monitoring and reporting are carried out by inspectors designated by the contracting parties;
that inspectors carry out inspections in the ports of the contracting countries.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 30 June 2012.
BACKGROUND
The EU is a party to the Convention on the International Conservation of Tunas.
For more information, see:
Bluefin tuna (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Caging vessel: a vessel used for the capture, transport or release of tuna in a cage or trap.
* Transfer: a transfer of a fish from a caged vessel or a trap into the ocean.

Summary 53:
Shipbuilding Injurious pricing: injurious pricing of ships
Shipbuilding injuriously priced ships
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2016/1036 on the enforcement of the Shipbuilding Injunctive Pricing Code
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EC) No 385/96 on the protection against sales of ships below their normal value which cause injury.
It aims to ensure a fair comparison between the export price and the normal value of ships sold to a buyer of the exporting country.
KEY POINTS
Injunctive pricing:
a ship is considered as being injurious priced if:
the export price of the vessel sold is less than a comparable price for a like vessel, in the ordinary course of trade, when sold to buyers of the importing country;
the normal value is calculated on the basis of the cost of production in the country of origin plus a reasonable amount for selling, general and administrative costs and for profits.
A shipbuilder is liable to be held liable for any damage caused by the sale of a vessel below its normal value.
The European Commission may initiate proceedings against a shipbuilder if it considers that further sales at less than normal value are imminent and that, unless protective action is taken, material injury will occur.
Complaints may be submitted by any natural or legal person, or any association not having legal personality, acting on behalf of the Union industry. The complaint may also contain a request for a hearing by an interested party who is likely to be affected by the result of the proceedings and who has particular reasons why they should be heard.
Annex I to Annex II to the regulation lists the factors, including contractual penalties, which may affect prices and price comparability.
If the shipbuilder concerned does not pay the injurious price imposed under Article 7, countermeasures under the form of denial of loading and unloading rights shall be imposed by the Commission on the vessels built by that shipbuilder in question.
Implementation of the regulation
The Commission may decide to open an investigation or proceedings if it is satisfied that a member of the allegedly injured Union industry met the criteria referred to in paragraph 3 (d), to justify such proceedings. The investigation may be concluded no later than 1 year from the date of initiation. It may also be terminated without any further measures being taken.
Provisional or final findings, affirmative or negative, may be made based on the facts available.
In the event that any interested party refuses access to, or otherwise does not provide the necessary information within the time limits provided for in this regulation, or significantly impedes the investigation, provisional or final conclusions may not be made.
Where measures are unnecessary, the proceedings may be terminated.

Summary 54:
Cableway installations — conformity assessment and conformity assessment procedures (Regulation (EC) No 765/2008 on subsystems and safety components of cableways and cableways in the European Union (EU) (see summary)
Cableways — conformity assessments and conformity assessments
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2000/9/EC on the ‘new approach’ principles on technical harmonisation and standards
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the conformity assessment* and conformity-assessment* procedures for subsystems* and components* of cableway installations.
It aims to ensure that the components and subsystems that are placed on the EU market comply with the requirements and that manufacturers have carried out the appropriate conformity assessment procedure.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all cableways, including:
cableways installed in the EU;
subsystems or safety components intended for use on cableways;
cabling systems intended for cableways.
Importers must ensure that:
the subsystem or safety component they place on the market meets the requirements;
the manufacturer has carried out a conformity assessment; and
the safety analysis has been carried out by the manufacturer.
Manufacturers must:
operate an approved quality system for production, final product inspection and testing of the subsystems, safety components and sub-systems concerned;
ensure that the safety analysis is carried out in accordance with the manufacturer’s’ specifications;
have an authorised representative, who is responsible for the safe operation of the installation;
assessentially carry out a safety analysis before placing a subsystem or a safety component on the European market.
importers are responsible for:
monitoring and control of the safety of subsystems;
checking that the sub-subsystem and safety component are in compliance with the relevant EU safety requirements.
The European Commission may adopt measures to prevent, detect and penalise infringements of the regulation. These measures must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
Inspections
The Commission must carry out regular inspections of the components concerned. It must also carry out periodic safety inspections of sub-sections and safety tests of safety components.
Where a sub- or safety part presents a risk, importers must immediately inform the competent national authorities of the EU countries in which they made the subsystem or the safety component available on sale to that effect, giving details, in particular, of the non-compliance and of any corrective measures taken.
If the Commission considers a measure taken by an EU country to be contrary to EU legislation, it must evaluate the national measure and take appropriate corrective measures.
EU countries must also ensure that all components from non-EU countries entering the EU are subject to the same surveillance and control procedures as those applicable to those from the EU.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2009.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Conformity assessment procedure: the procedure in which a product is tested to ensure it meets all the essential requirements of EU legislation.
* Safety analysis: the process in which an organisation or a body assesses whether a component meets the essential safety requirements of the relevant legislation and, if it does not, takes corrective measures to ensure its safety.

Summary 55:
Accessibility of products and services for persons with disabilities
Assessment of accessibility requirements for goods and services in the internal market — Directive 2011/43/EU
Assessing of accessibility obligations for products, services and information
SUMMARY OF:
Directive 2011/42/EU on the accessibility of products, goods and information for persons who are blind or visually impaired
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It aims to improve the level of protection of persons with disability in the European Union (EU) market by ensuring that products, products and information are accessible to people with disabilities.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The directive applies to:
electronic ticketing services, electronic tickets and interactive self-service terminals;
services providing access to audiovisual media services, including mobile applications developed or made available by operators of passenger transport services within the scope of this directive or on their behalf;
information services, such as websites, mobile device-based services, e-ticketing services and electronic tickets.
It does not apply to the provision of information services.
The European Commission is assisted by a committee composed of representatives of EU countries and chaired by the European Parliament and the Council.
EU countries must ensure that:
all EU citizens, regardless of their abilities, can enjoy the benefits of the directive’s accessibility requirements;
people with disabilities have access to the information and services offered within the EU, including:
the information and information provided on the internet;
the electronic ticketing service;
accessibility of the information provided by the operator;
online ticketing;
service providers.
Manufacturers, importers and importers must ensure the information they provide is accessible to persons who have disabilities;
businesses and microenterprises are required to ensure that their products are accessible.
Obligations of manufacturers and economic operators dealing with products
Manufacturer and importer must:
ensure that products they have placed on the market comply with the accessibility requirements set out in the directive;
make sure that the CE marking is affixed visibly, legibly and legibly on their products;
provide the European Commission with a description of the products and the services they offer;
assess the products they offer and provide the Commission with an explanation of the reasons for their non-compliance.
If a product is found to be non-compliant, EU countries must take the necessary measures to ensure it is withdrawn from their market, and inform the Commission accordingly.
In addition, the Commission must establish appropriate control mechanisms such as a posteriori control by the market surveillance authorities, in order to verify that the exemption from the disability requirements application is justified.
Where a product does not comply with this directive, the manufacturer or importer may withdraw it from the market and notify the Commission of the reason for the decision. The Commission must then take appropriate measures, including the withdrawal of the product from the EU market, in accordance with the rules laid down in the annex to the directive.
Annex II to the Directive sets out the responsibilities of economic operators.
Economic operators must ensure:
that:
information and communication services are accessible;
that information and communications are provided in a manner which is accessible; and
that the information, communication and communication service providers provide information in a way that is accessible, including in written and oral format.
They must also ensure that information and communication providers provide training on:
access to information;
transport services;
public transport;
internet access;
e-tourist information services, i.e. the information that can be provided on a website or on a mobile application;
mobile applications;
radio and television programmes;
webcasts;
audio-visual media services and e-texts;
telecommunications service providers providing information on the services offered.
Information services and webcasts must be provided in such a way as to enable users to make use of the services provided.
Internet access must be accessible to users with disabilities by means of:
an electronic programme guide (EPG) which is perceivable, operable, electronic communications service providers to the most appropriate PSAP;
visual programme guides which are perceivable and operable;
a user-friendly PSAP which is capable of displaying information in an easily accessible manner;
an interactive PSAP with a Braille display so that blind persons can use the computer;
navigational assistance for users who are visually impaired.
Technical specifications for products
Products must meet the following requirements:
they must be able to be read and understood;
they should have a visible, legible and legible interface;
there should be a refreshable Braille or tactile display;
users should be provided with the possibility to refresh the Braille and tactile display so they can see the information displayed on the product;
products should have the ability to read and understand the technical specifications for the product.

Summary 56:
Controlling trade in minerals from conflict-affected and high-risk areas: responsible sourcing and third-party auditing
Containing trade in mineral and metal trade
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on the control of trade in certain minerals and metals from conflict areas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to prevent and combat the financing of armed groups* and the illegal exploitation of minerals.
It sets out the obligations of EU importers of minerals* and metals to ensure that the vast majority, but no less than 95 %, of the total volumes imported into the EU of each mineral or metal under the Combined Nomenclature code is subject to the obligations set out in this regulation.
The regulation applies from 1 January 2021.
KEY POINTS
EU importers must:
ensure that:
they carry out audits of their own supply chain due diligence via an independent third party in accordance with Article 6(1) of this regulation;
they register the names and addresses of global responsible smelters and refiners, including those listed in the regulation’s annexes;
check that they have carried out independent audits of the supply chain of the minerals they import;
carry out periodic checks of the relevant supply chain traceability schemes.
They must keep records of these checks for at least 5 years.
Importers must also:
identify the names, addresses and contact details of the companies responsible for the supply of minerals;
assess the impact of the regulation on the regulation, including the impact on small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and on their competitiveness;
draw up a register of responsible producers and importers;
make available to the public a list of the global responsible producers, importers and exporters of metals.
This regulation applies to:
mineral and metal importers’ annual import volume;
the total volume of minerals or metals they import into the European Union (EU);
the volume of metals they export to the EU that they export;
minerates of minerals, metals and minerals traded in the EU.
In addition, the regulation sets out:
the rules and general principles concerning mechanisms for control by EU countries of the European Commission’'s exercise of implementing powers;
a list of EU-wide responsible producers;
rules for the management of the register of EU countries’ responsible importers.
EU countries must ensure that they:
recognise recognised schemes for the responsible sourcing of minerals by the EU;
take the necessary measures to ensure the traceability and traceability of minerals imported into their territory;
monitor the compliance of the recognised schemes;
report to the Commission every 5 years on the cost of responsible sourcing, the administrative consequences of such sourcing and auditing and their potential impact on competitiveness, in particular that of SMEs, and should report its findings to the European Parliament and to the Council.
If the Commission considers that the regulation does not meet its objectives, it may adopt delegated acts to amend the regulation. These amendments may include:
an amendment to the annex to the regulation concerning the definition of conflict minerals,
the definition of ‘conflict minerals’,
a revision of the definitions of conflict and illegal exploitation minerals, and
a regulation on traceability.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2011 and had to become law in the Member States by 1 January 2020.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Conflict minerals: minerals that have been mined or mined in conflict areas.
* Conflict minerals: those that are mined, mined or extracted by armed groups, which are often linked to conflicts in the Middle East, North Africa, South Asia and the Pacific.

Summary 57:
Customs status of goods — release, verification, release and disposal of goods (Regulation (EC) No 867/2013)
Customs Status of goods – Release, Verification, Release and Disposition of Goods (Recast)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules on the status and release of goods placed under customs supervision.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to goods that are imported into the European Union (EU) and exported out of the EU.
It does not apply to goods imported from non-EU countries.
EU countries may designate parts of the customs territory of the Union as free zones.
The rules apply to:
non-EU goods;
goods imported from outside the EU;
the goods exported from the EU to the EU or exported to the European Economic Area (EEA).
The European Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts, in accordance with Article 284 of the regulation, in order to adopt implementing acts. These implementing acts must be adopted by the Commission and must comply with the implementing acts referred to in Article 285(4) of the implementing act.
In addition, the Commission must adopt implementing measures to ensure that:
the customs authorities do not fail to act in the interests of public morality, public policy or public security,
the protection of the health and life of humans, animals or plants, the environment, the protection of national treasures, and the protection against such prohibitions and restrictions as are justified on grounds of, inter alia, public morality or public policy, public security.
Duty exemption or reduced rate of duty
The Commission may grant a duty exemption or reduce the duty exemption if:
in the case of prior export or prior import;
in cases of prior import or prior export, the customs authorities may exempt the goods from duty;
when a debtor fails to pay the import or export duty payable, the debtor may be entitled to a reduction in the amount of the duty payable.
Repayment and remission
The debtor is entitled to repay the customs duty payable within 14 days of the expiry of the period concerned. The debtor may extend that period upon application by the debtor where the amount has been determined in the course of post-release control, or if the debtor was acting in good faith.
If the debtor does not pay the duty, it may be liable to be repaid by the person who abandons the goods to the State. The payment may be made by a third person instead of the debtor. The costs incurred must be borne by the declarant.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 31 December 2013 and had to become law in the EU countries by 31 December 2020.
BACKGROUND
 
For more information, see:
‘Customs’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Customs status: the legal status of a goods under customs control.

Summary 58:
Ensuring intellectual property rights are enforced throughout the European Union (EU) (Regulation (EC) No 1383/2003).
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2015/849 on intellectual property enforcement
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a system for the enforcement of intellectual property (IP) rights by customs authorities in the European Economic Area (EEA).
It sets out the procedures for applying to customs authorities for enforcement of IP rights.
KEY POINTS
EU applications
A European Union application may be submitted only with respect to intellectual property based on EU law producing effects throughout the EU. Applications must be submitted to the competent customs department of an EU country and must contain all the information required by Article 6(3) of the regulation. Where a new intellectual property right is added, the request must contain the information referred to in points (c), (e), (g), (h) and (i) of that decision.
The applicant must provide the customs authorities with:
a copy of the application;
a description of the goods concerned;
the name and address of the person or entity responsible for the infringement;
an explanation of the nature and nature of the infringement.
If the customs department considers that the application does not contain all information required, it will request the applicant to supply the missing information within 10 working days of notification of the request. If the applicant does not comply with the request, the goods will be held under a suspensive procedure or placed in a free zone or free warehouse. The conditions under which the goods can be released for free circulation shall be determined by the authorities;
brought out of the customs territory of the EU;
exported;
re-exported,
placed free circulation.
Customs actions
The customs authorities may take action in the following cases:
in the event of infringements of an IP right;
in relation to the destruction of goods in small consignments;
where the goods are in possession of persons or entities who are suspected of infringing the intellectual property of another EU country.
These actions must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive. They must be carried out under customs control.
In addition, the European Commission must establish a central electronic database containing information relating to decisions on applications and to customs actions. The database must be maintained for 6 months after proceedings have determined in a final way whether an intellectual property has been infringed.
Implementation
The Commission shall establish an extension request form by means of implementing acts. The Commission must inform the European Parliament, the Council and the Commission of any measures taken to extend the expiry of the period for applying for an EU application. The extension request must be made within 2 months of the date on which the EU application was submitted and in all other EU countries where action is requested the day following the date in which the request was requested.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATING APPLY?
 
    Егалка  
It has applied since 1 January 2015.
BACKGROUND
  Жбала 
For more information, see:
EU Intellectual Property Rights (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Intellectual property right: a legal right that protects a product or service from being copied or reproduced.
* Small consignment: a consignment of goods of less than 10 kg.

Summary 59:
Customs programme: 2021-2021
Customs Programme: 2021 - 2021
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1046 — Customs programme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a customs programme at EU level.
It sets up a multiannual framework for cooperation between EU countries’ customs authorities and the European Commission on customs and customs control equipment.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies from 1 January 2021 to 31 December 2023.
Objectives
The objectives of the programme are to:
promote cooperation between the customs authorities or economic operators concerned to make full and effective use of the European electronic systems;
improve the interoperability of national customs and economic operators’ systems with the European Union’s electronic systems.
To achieve these objectives, the programme is implemented by the Commission under the Customs programme (‘the Programme’).
The programme is aligned to the multiannually financial framework of the EU. It is funded by the general budget of the Union.
Awards, complementarity and combined funding
The European Commission is responsible for administering the programme.
The Commission is assisted by an expert group composed of representatives of EU countries and appointed in their personal capacity and required to act independently and in the public interest. The objective of ensuring a balanced representation of stakeholders and the principle of gender equality should be taken into account when selecting external experts.
Exercises of the delegated acts
Commission Delegated acts are adopted by the European Parliament and the Council of the Commission.

Summary 60:
The European Social Fund (ESF+)
The European social fund (ESA)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2021/694 establishing the European social Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the EU’s social fund for the period 2021-2027.
It aims to support Member States and regions to achieve high employment levels, fair social protection and a skilled and resilient workforce ready for the future world of work, as well as inclusive and cohesive societies aiming to eradicating poverty and delivering on the principles set out in the European Pillar of Social Rights.
KEY POINTS
The ESF+ aims to:
promote flexible opportunities for upgrading of skills and acquiring new and different skills by all, in particular entrepreneurial and digital skills, skills for key enabling technologies and skills for the green economy and industrial ecosystems in line with the Commission communication of 10 March 2020 entitled ‘A New Industrial Strategy for Europe’.
support for social innovation and social entrepreneurship in order to encourage and support innovative solutions.
Promote the social inclusion of non-EU nationals, particularly women and people from developing countries.
Support for social entrepreneurship and social innovation in the context of the European Union (EU) 2020-2025 strategy.
In order to achieve these objectives, the ESF will:
support the creation of networks of social entrepreneurs and social entrepreneurs;
encourage the development of innovative solutions;
support social entrepreneurship;
provide financial support for social entrepreneurs.
The EU countries and regions with the necessary to implement social entrepreneurship strategies. These strategies should be presented alongside the yearly national reform programmes.
Eligibility
Member States will allocate at least 25% of their resources to the specific objectives for the social and employment policy area set out by the regulation, including the promotion of the socio-economic integration of third-country nationals. The European Commission may also allocate up to 25 % of its resources under shared management to specific objectives, including:
the social inclusion policy area;
promoting the inclusion of women and men in the labour market;
the promotion of social entrepreneurship, including entrepreneurship and innovation;
improving the quality of education and training;
raising awareness of the importance of the right skill sets and employment and social policies and actions.
Specific objectives
The regulation sets out the general objectives of ESF+. These include:
raising employment levels;
increasing the participation of women in labour markets;
ensuring equal opportunities and access to labour market and fair working conditions;
protecting the rights of the most deprived persons;
developing the skills and knowledge of young people;
enhancing the knowledge and skills of people with disabilities;
creating an environment for innovation and entrepreneurship; and
encouraging and supporting social entrepreneurship.
Funding
The financial envelope for the implementation of the ESA is € 87 995 063 417, in 2018 prices. This covers the period from 2021 to 2027. It is divided into 4 strands:
social inclusion strand:
education, training, employment and skills;
employment and social protection strand;
education and training strand: education, training and employment;
social entrepreneurship strand: skills and training, entrepreneurship, social innovation, and innovation.
Social innovation strand: the social entrepreneurship strand, which aims to promote the social innovation of the social entrepreneur, social entrepreneur and social entrepreneur. The social entrepreneur strand includes:
creative and digital solutions, skills and technology-based solutions, and the social entrepreneurial strand.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
European Social Fund
European social fund
European Parliament and Council Regulation (EC) No 883/2013 of 21 December 2013 on the establishment of the Social Fund.
See consolidated version.

The Social Fund and the European Regional Development Fund (European Commission).

Summary 61:
EU solidarity programme 2021-2027 — rules on cross-border volunteering and volunteering for young people with fewer opportunities (European Voluntary Service)
EU solidarity program 2021 - 2027 – rules on crossing borders
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/817 on the European Union solidarity programme for the period from 2021 to 2027
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules on the EU solidarity programme (EU solidarity) for 2021–2027.
It aims to encourage young Europeans to express their solidarity in practice by participating in solidarity activities across borders.
KEY POINTS
The objectives of the programme are to:
raise awareness of the importance of solidarity and human rights;
encourage the participation of young people in humanitarian crises and their aftermath;
contribute to strengthening the resilience and capacity of vulnerable or disaster-affected communities to cope with and recover from crises;
promote the application of the Charter of Fundamental Rights and the principles of equality between men and women and the right to non-discrimination based on sex, racial or ethnic origin, religion or belief, disability, age or sexual orientation, socioeconomic background, and to promote international humanitarian law.
Participation of individuals
The programme is open to young people from the public, private and non-governmental organisations (NGOs) in the solidarity, non-profit and youth sectors, as well as to existing networks at EU level relevant to the activities.
Organisations that wish to offer solidarity activities under the programme must first receive a quality label from the European Commission.
The European Commission is assisted by a steering committee composed of representatives from the EU countries and the European Social Fund.
EU countries may only participate in the programme in its entirety and provided that they fulfil all the obligations which this regulation imposes on Member States in point (c) of the first subparagraph of Article 62(1) of that regulation.
In addition, Member States must:
ensure that national authorities respect the principles and principles of equal treatment of men, women and children;
provide training and guidance to volunteers;
support the development and capacity-building components of the volunteering, thereby strengthening local networks and communities.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The EU’s solidarity programme is one of the main instruments of the Erasmus+ programme, which aims to strengthen the solidarity of young Europeans in the face of social and economic challenges.
For more information, see:
European Union solidarity (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
Cross-border solidarity: volunteering undertaken by young people across borders in the context of a crisis or their aftermath.
Youth: young people who are active in the social, political, economic and cultural life of an EU country.
Non-governmental organisation: an organisation that is not a member of the EU.

Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2019/821 of 21 December 2019 on the implementation of Regulation (EC) No 1288/2013 of the European Parliament and of the Council relating to the European Voluntary Services (European Union Solidarity Programme for 2021 – 2027) (OJ L 248, 28.12.2019, pp. 1-8)

Summary 62:
Equal Opportunities Fund (EGF)
Equitable opportunities for women
Equality for men and women
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 883/2013 on the European Equal Opportunities Facility
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It establishes the European equal opportunities fund (EGF).
It aims to eliminate inequalities and promote equal opportunities between men* and women in order to combat discrimination based on sex, racial or ethnic origin, religion or belief, disability, age or sexual orientation.
KEY POINTS
The EGF’s main objectives are to:
promote equal opportunities for men, women and persons with disabilities;
combat gender pay gap;
encourage the retraining and requalification of women into employment or self-employment.
The objectives of the EGF are set out in the Regulation (EU) 2016/679 on the Multiannual Financial Framework for a European Union that delivers efficiently on its priorities post-2020.
Eligible measures
EU countries may apply for EGF funding for measures in line with the EU Quality Framework for Employment, Social Affairs and Inclusion (QF2020) and national programmes in accordance with the objectives laid down in Annex II of the Regulation. These measures must reflect the prospective needs of the local or regional labour market.
Beneficiary surveys
The European Commission must conduct a beneficiary survey every 2 years. The survey must be open to participants for at least 4 weeks and should be launched during the 6 months after the end of the implementation period. It should identify potential cases for intervention at an early stage. The results should be based on:
the number of unemployed, inactive, employed and self-employed people;
the percentage of jobs that require lower qualifications.
In order to support beneficiaries effectively and rapidly, EU countries should do their utmost to submit complete applications when applying for a financial contribution from the European Union (EU).
The Commission must ensure that the results of the survey are submitted to the European Parliament and the Council of the EU within 3 months of its completion. The Commission is assisted by a committee composed of representatives of the Member States and chaired by the European Commission.
Management and financial control
The Fund is managed by the Commission, assisted by an advisory committee. It is supervised by a director-general. It must:
ensure that the Commission implements technical assistance under indirect management;
identify the third party responsible for carrying out the tasks assigned to it according to the Financial Regulation.
It must also ensure that beneficiaries’ data are collected and processed according to EU data protection rules.
If the Commission considers that a measure does not comply with the rules, it must inform the Member State concerned. If no agreement has been reached, the Commission may, within 12 months of receipt of the observations, make the financial corrections required by cancelling all or part of the financial contribution of the fund to the measure in question.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 20 July 1998 and had to become law in the EU countries by 20 July 2000.
BACKGROUND
 
The EU‘s Equal Opportunity Fund is one of the main instruments of the European Pillar of Social Rights. It was set up following the financial crisis of the global financial and economic crisis.
For more information, see:
Gender Equality Fund (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Gender pay gap: the difference between the average hourly rate of pay between a man and a woman for the same work performed by the same job.
* Unemployed person: a person who is not employed but who has the right to be employed.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC) No 802/2013/2013 of 20 July 2013 establishing a European equal opportunity fund for women and men (OJ L 127, 20.8.2013, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EEC) no 802/13/2013 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 63:
Registration of interest representatives in the European Union’s public procurement register
Registration of interests representatives
SUMMARY OF:
Agreement between the European Parliament, the Council, the European Commission and the European Economic and Social Committee on the establishment of the European Public Procurement Register (EPSR)
Decision (EU) 2016/852 — conclusion of the Agreement between the EU institutions, bodies, offices and agencies and the management board of the EPSR
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND OF THE DECISION?
The agreement establishes a register for interest representatives* who wish to participate in the decision-making processes of the signatory institutions.
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Eligibility and code of conduct
Applicants for registration in the register must meet the following criteria:
be an EU citizen;
be a legal resident of an EU Member State;
have a minimum age of 18;
not be a member of an interest group.
Once an applicant has been activated, the applicant must become a registrant in accordance with the rules set out in the agreement.
Applicant must be:
an EU citizen or a permanent resident of the Member States;
a legal resident or resident of a Member State that is a party to an EU institution, body, office or agency;
participate in the activities covered by the agreement;
engage in activities that may affect the formulation or implementation of EU policy or legislation;
represent the interests of the institutions or bodies, bodies or agencies concerned;
the activities of interest groups, bodies and agencies.
A registrants may be excluded from the agreement if:
they are ineligible;
they have not met the criteria set out above;
their activities do not conform with the principles of transparency and ethical representation;
there is a risk that they may be involved in illegal activities that could undermine the integrity of the public procurement process.
An applicant may be ineligible if they:
have not complied with the conditions of the agreement,
have committed a serious offence;
are not complying with the requirements of the regulation;
contribute to the financing of illegal activities or activities that are contrary to the objectives of the register.
Ineligibility
The management board (‘Management Board’) consists of the Secretaries-General of the member institutions, who will chair it on a rotating basis for a term of one the applicant shall become a registerrant.
Member States may decide to make certain activities conditional upon registration. They must notify the Management Board of the measures by means of which they decide to do so, or of any complementary transparency measures that they take. The Management Board may also adopt conditionality or complementary measures to encourage registration and strengthen the joint framework established by this agreement and that they reinforce the objective of the coordinated approach referred to in Article 1, namely, to set a high standard of transparent and ethical interest representation at EU level.
Monitoring, investigations and investigations
The Management Board must:
monitor and investigate all activities carried out by interest representatives with the aim of influencing EU policy;
ensure that the information submitted by them is accurate;
conduct itself in line with the agreement and the rules of conduct set out therein;
identify, monitor and investigate any irregularities or irregularities that may occur;
draw up a list of persons with authorisation to access the premises of the Union institutions and bodies.
If an applicant fails to comply with the above conditions, the Secretariat must open an investigation and notify the complainant and the registrant concerned.
Complaints must be submitted in writing. If a complaint is found to be admissible, it must be forwarded to the European Court of Justice (ECJ).
The ECJ may, on its own initiative, open its own investigation and decide to impose sanctions on the applicant.
FROM WHEN DO THE DECISIONS APPLY?
Decisions 2016 and 2016 have applied since 1 January 2016.
BACKGROUND
The European Parliament and the Council have adopted a number of measures to improve the transparency of public procurement in the EU, including:
the establishment of a register of interested persons (e.g. interest groups);
the setting up of a management board.
For more information, see:
‘The European Public procurement register’ on the EPPR's website.
MAIN DOCUMENTS
Council Decision (EU), Euratom and European Parliament of 21 December 2016 on the conclusion of an Agreement between Member States, of the one part, and The European Commission, of its Member States and of the Council of 26 December 2014 on establishing the European public procurement registry (OJ L 263, 28.12.2016, pp. 1-8)
Council decision (EU, Euratom, European Economic & Social Committee) 2016-852 of 27 December 2016 concerning the conclusion, on behalf thereof, of an agreement between the Member State and



Summary 64:
Budgetary agreement between the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union (EU) 2021-2027 — financial rules applicable to the general budget of the EU (MFF 2021 to 2027)
BUDGET AGREEMENT
Budget Agreement between the EU institutions and the European Commission
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU, Euratom) 2018/1046 on the conclusion, on behalf of the Union, of an agreement between European Parliament, the Council and the Commission on the budgetary rules applicable in the multiannual financial framework for the years 2021 to 2020
Agreement on the implementation of budgetary discipline, to improve the functioning of the annual budgetary procedure and cooperation between the Institutions on budgetary matters as well as to ensure sound financial management
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE AGREEEMENT?
The decision approves the conclusion of the agreement on the basis of a proposal from the Commission.
The agreement establishes a roadmap towards the introduction of new own resources that are sufficient to cover the repayment of a European Union Recovery Instrument established under Council Regulation (EU), the EURI Regulation (the "EURI Regulation").
The annexes to this agreement form an integral part of the regulation.
KEY POINTS
The European Union’s budgetary rules apply to:
the general budget;
the annual budgetary programme; and
the European Union recovery instrument (EURI);
the own resources.
In addition, the Commission must:
implement budgetary discipline;
ensure that its own resources are not over-spent;
are not overspentestimated;
use the instruments referred to in the Regulation and the Annexes to the MFFSPSP expenditure which is charged to of instruments referred in the regulation and in this agreement.
Cooperation between the institutions
The Commission and the institutions must ensure that:
budgetary procedures are implemented in line with EU law;
all budgetary lines are classified by budgetary nomenclature;
there are regular meetings of the budgetary committees and trilogues to discuss budgetary matters;
budgeting is carried out by the Commission and by the institutions in accordance with the rules of the Regulation on budgetary discipline and the annex to the agreement;
each institution must submit a report to the Commission every year on its financial position;
a report is sent to the EU Parliament and to the Council every 2 years on the financial position of the institutions;
an annual legislative work programme is published in the annual legislative programme;
regular meetings are held alternately at the premises of the Parliament and of the Council, with a view to an equal sharing of facilities, including interpretation facilities.
SOUND FINANCIAL MANAGEMENT OF UNION FUNDS
The EU institutions must implement budgetary discipline:
to ensure that the budget is balanced;
to implement the rules on the use of the own resources;
inform the Commission of any changes in the EU budget that could have a financial impact on the budget; and,
to examine the scope for reallocating appropriations.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DECISION APPLY?
It has applied since 18 July 2018.
BACKGROUND
   
The MFF 2021–2027 is the first financial framework to be adopted by the EU. It covers the period from 2021 until 2027.
For more information, see:
European Union budget (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Own resources: financial instruments that are charged to the European Fund for Strategic Partnerships (CFSP).
CFSP expenditure: the amount of money that a body receives from the CFSP to cover its own expenses.

Summary 65:
Economic support for the COVID-19 crisis: financial instruments
Economic support to the EU’s economic recovery
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2018/1046 — financial instruments for the economic recovery of the European Union (EU)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a financial instrument to support economic recovery in the EU in the wake of COVID (Coordinated intervention in the internal market for goods and services in response to the exceptional situation caused by COVID 19).
KEY POINTS
The COVID crisis has caused significant disturbances to economic activity which are reflected in a steep decline in gross domestic product (GDP) and a significant impact on employment, social conditions, poverty and inequalities. A sharp contraction of growth in the Union is foreseen for 2020.
To ensure a sustainable and resilient recovery throughout the EU and facilitate the implementation of economic support, the established mechanisms of spending through EU programmes under the multiannual financial framework are to be used.
The financial instruments to be financed under this regulation are:
non-repayable support, support through financial instruments or provisioning for budgetary guarantees and related expenditure by the EU;
investment in rural areas in addressing the impact of the crisis;
financial commitments giving rise to expenditure for support, technical and administrative assistance for implementation of the measures set out in the instrument;
the provision of budgetary guarantees up to an amount of € 384 400 million in 2018 prices.
Financing of the Instrument and allocation of funds
The instruments are financed on the basis of the empowerment provided for in Article 5 of the own resources decision of the EU Parliament and of the Council.
EU countries’ own resources are to use the financial instruments provided for by the Regulation on the financing of their own resources.
In view of the nature of the instruments, one part of the amounts available under the Instrument should be used for loans to EU countries, whereas the other part of these amounts should constitute external assigned revenue for the purpose of Article 21(5) of Regulation (EU), Euratom, 2018/946.
Implementation of the financial instrument
The measures to be implemented under the instrument are to:
recover the costs of the exceptional measures taken by EU countries to respond to COVID;
ensure that the measures are implemented in line with the principles of sound economic management;
support the efforts of the Commission and the Member States to implement the measures taken under this instrument.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 31 December 2018.
BACKGROUND
 
The crisis caused a sharp contraction in the economic activity of the Union in the period between 1 January 2014 and 31 December 2020, which has led to a sharp decline in GDP and a severe deterioration in the financial situation of many businesses.
For more information, see:
‘Economic support’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 66:
Stabilisation and growth pact
Stepping up surveillance of national economic policies
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1466/97 on measures to safeguard the stability and growth of the euro area
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the enforcement of the Stability and Growth Pact (SGP) in the European Union (EU).
The SGP allows the EU to adopt specific measures in euro area countries which go beyond the provisions applicable to all EU countries, for the purpose of ensuring the proper functioning of the economic and monetary union.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
the prevention and corrective parts of the SGP;
the stabilisation part of the Stabilisation & Growth Pact.
Sanctions in the preventive part
EU countries must lodge with the European Commission a non-interest-bearing deposit amounting to 0.2 % of their gross domestic product (GDP) of the GDP in the preceding year. The deposit must bear an interest rate reflecting the Commission’s credit risk and the relevant investment period. The Commission may, on grounds of exceptional economic circumstances or following a reasoned request by the EU country concerned addressed to the Commission, recommend that the Council reduce the amount of the fine or cancel it. If the Council adopts a decision establishing that a Member State failed to take action in response to the Council recommendation, the Commission must, by a further decision, require the Member State in question to lodge with its interest-bearing deposits. The interest accrued thereon must be made up the shortfall when it lodges the deposit.
the Commission must:
make up the difference between the interest accrued and the amount lodged in accordance with Article 4 of the regulation;
ensure that the Commission carries out appropriate consultations during its investigations;
take appropriate measures to prevent the manipulation of statistics.
The Commission is empowered to adopt delegated acts in respect of:
detailed criteria for establishing the fine and for conducting the investigations,
the amount of fine and the associated procedures for the investigation, and
the legal representation of EU countries in the investigations.
In the corrective part, EU countries must ensure that:
their budgetary consolidation measures are implemented;
their economic policies are in line with the medium-term budgetary objective;
they comply with the rules on budgetary consolidation laid down in the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU (TFEU);
they take all necessary measures to ensure that their economic policies conform with the budgetary objective.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 1998.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
 * Stabilization and Growth pact: a set of rules designed to ensure the stability of economic policies of euro-area countries in order to ensure their long-term economic and financial stability.
* Stability and growth Pact: a series of measures designed to prevent and correct any serious deterioration in the economic situation of euro countries.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU) No 2014/97 of 21 December 1997 on measures in the framework of the Security and Growth Partnership (SSP) (OJ L 183, 1.1.1998, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 1465/97 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

  The European Commission adopted a communication to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions on the implementation of the Statute of the European Central Bank in the field of the Single Supervisory Mechanism (SSM) (COM(2014) 696 final, 31.12.2014)

Summary 67:
Population and housing statistics
Statistics
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 284/2003 on the collection of statistics on the population and the main family, social, economic and housing characteristics of persons
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the methodology, definitions and programme of the statistical data and the metadata for population and housing censuses in the European Union (EU).
It establishes a reference year for each EU country and sets out a programme of data and metadata to be transmitted to the European Commission (Eurostat).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries. It covers the population, families and households, as well as on housing at a national, regional and local level, as set out in the annex to the regulation.
It applies to:
the population of the EU;
the main family and social, social and economic characteristics of households;
housing characteristics;
a combination of register-based, sample surveys and conventional censuses;
appropriate surveys with rotating samples (rolling censuses).
EU countries must take all measures necessary to meet the requirements of data protection.
Data sources and methodologies
The European Commission is responsible for the management of the data sources and methods used for the collection and transmission of the statistics. It is assisted by the European Statistical Programme Committee.
The Commission:
contains representatives of the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions;
is assisted by Eurostat.
Eurostat:
is responsible for collecting, processing and transmitting the data;
provides Eurostat’s statistical data in electronic form;
assists the Commission in the preparation and dissemination of statistical data to Eurostat and Eurostat in the field of population, family and housing;
publishes the results of the national and regional population and household surveys;
conducts surveys on the characteristics of the population;
ensures that the data it collects are reliable, reliable, relevance, cost-effectiveness and statistical confidentiality;
regularly reports on the quality of the collected data and on the methods used;
reports to the Commission on the reliability, reliability, relevance and statistical accuracy of the results.
Programme of data
The national authorities must:
ensure that Eurostat has the necessary data sources, methods and metadata;
identify the sources and methodology that meet the essential features of population* and housing* censuses as defined in Article 2 of the regulation;
designate a programme for the transmission of data, the metadata and the verification of the validated data and data sources;
establish the reference years, the methodology and the programme;
verify the quality and reliability of the metadata.
In addition, Eurostat must report on the extent to which the chosen data sources or methodology meet the necessary features of these essential features.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
Council Regulation (EU) No 282/2003 has applied since 20 December 2003.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
‘Censuses’ on Eurostat's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Population: the number of people who are considered to be residents of an EU country.
Housing characteristics: the main characteristics of a household, such as income, employment, education, age, occupation, gender, age of children and residence.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision 2004/852/EC of 20 November 2004 on the establishment of the reference year (OJ L 284, 20.12.2004, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Decision 2004 /852 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 68:
Rules of Procedure for the 9th parliamentary term of the European Union (EU) (2019-2022) (Official Journal L 302 of 22.11.2019)
Rules of Procedures for the ninth parliamentary term
SUMMARY OF:
RULES OF PROCEDURE
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATIONS?
The rules of procedure laid down by the European Parliament (Parliament) for its 9th Parliamentary term are designed to ensure the smooth functioning of the EU’s internal market and the efficient functioning of its internal market.
They aim to:
ensure the proper functioning of Parliament;
facilitate the exchange of information between political parties;
improve the efficiency and effectiveness of the internal market; and
improve transparency.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The Rules of Procedure cover:
legislative acts;
procedures for the adoption, adoption and implementation of legally binding acts.
The procedure for the approval, adoption, implementation and adoption of legislative acts is laid down in the rules of Procedure L 302, which are published in the Official Journal of the Union (OJ L 302).
The procedures for the implementation of legislation are set out in the annex to the rules. The annexes to the annexes include:
the rules concerning the reimbursement of incurred costs;
the procedures for:
approval, approval, approval and implementation;
implementation;
consultation;
reconclusions;
exchange of views;
interinstitutional agreements.
Rules concerning the officers of Parliament
The Parliament must elect a President, a Vice-President and a Quaestor. The president and vice-president are elected by secret ballot. The President must inform the Council and the Commission of the positions taken under this rule. If it becomes necessary for the President to be replaced, a successor must be elected in accordance with the respective rules for elections to the office concerned.
Political parties may designate one of their members in each committee to be a coordinator. They may also designate one or more Vice-Chairs.
A proposal for a legislative act may be tabled jointly by up to 10 Members. It must be submitted to the committee responsible for drafting the legislative act. The committee responsible must, as soon as possible regardless of whether the recommendation from the committee is to approve or reject the act, and no amendments are tabled. If the committee recommends that the act be approved or rejected, it must submit a draft proposal to the president for debate and a vote. The draft proposal must contain:
a draft proposal;
an explanatory statement including, where appropriate, a financial statement;
a description of the draft legislative act;
details of the reasons for its adoption or adoption.
Amendments
Amending the act must be approved by a qualified majority of at least 75% of the Members of the Committee responsible. If a Member of the committee requests that the amendment be amended, the amendment must be presented to the full Parliament for a vote and the President must decide on the admissibility of such amendments. The amendment must not be more than 200 words long. The amendments must be made in writing and must be accompanied by an explanatory statement.
In the case of amendments, the amendments must comply with the following conditions:
they must be in the language of the law of the Member State in which they are to be adopted;
they should not contain any reference to the Member States’ laws, regulations or administrative rules;
their content must be clear and unambiguous.
If the committee considers that the amendments are not in line with these conditions, it may withdraw the act.
Implementing acts
The European Parliament adopts implementing acts in the light of the recommendations of the High Level Group on Gender Equality and Diversity on 11 April 2018. These implementing acts must be legally binding and have the necessary legal effect. They must be adopted by the Council, the European Commission and the European Economic and Social Committee (EEC) and must contain the following provisions:
an explanation of the legal basis for the decision;
rules concerning the procedure for implementing the implementing act. They include the right of the originating institution to withdraw the draft act and the right to amend it.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The new rules entered into force
1 July 2019.
REFERENCES
Act

Deadline for transposition into force in Member States
Official Journal
Regulation (EC) No 552/2014
-
-

Summary 69:
European Data Protection Supervisor (EDPS) — rules on the protection of personal data
European data Protection Supervisor
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2018/1725 establishing an independent authority responsible for ensuring that the fundamental rights and freedoms of natural persons, and in particular their right to data protection, are respected by the Union institutions, bodies, offices and agencies.
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the European data protection supervisor.
It sets out the tasks and powers of the EDPS.
KEY POINTS
The EDPS’s tasks are to:
ensure that:
the protection of the personal data of EU citizens is respected by EU institutions and bodies;
that the processing of their personal data is in line with the principles of data protection;
to ensure that the data protection of individuals is respected in all EU institutions; and
to protect the privacy and security of individuals’ personal data.
The director and the Appointing authority are appointed by the European Union Agency for Law Enforcement Cooperation (EDPB).
The Director is assisted by the Director of the European Data Protection Office (EDPO). The Director is responsible for:
coordinating the work of the Directorate-General for the Protection of the Data Protection of European Union (EDPEU);
ensuring the proper functioning of the secretariat of the Management Meeting;
assisting the Director in the appointment of the EDPB;
exercising the powers and duties of the Director.
In addition, the Director assists the Director-General to ensure consistency and overall coordination of EDPS and on any other tasks delegated to him or her by the EU data protection supervisory authorities, including:
monitoring, analysing, reviewing, investigating, investigating and prosecuting data breaches;
providing advice and assistance to the Director and to the EU agency for law enforcement cooperation;
advising the Director on the application of the EU law on data protection.
A staff committee is set up to advise and assist the Director, and to make recommendations on organisational matters and working conditions. The committee is composed of 3 members and 3 deputies, and elected for a period of 2 years.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
   
The European Union has adopted a number of measures to protect the rights of citizens. These include:
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2017/1939 establishing a European Union Data Protection Board (EDB);
Directive (EU), 2016/680 on the establishment of an independent data protection authority, referred to as the EU Data Protection Supervisory Supervisor;
Commission Implementing Decision of 11 May 2016 on the European EU Agency for law Enforcement Cooperation and replacing and repealing Council Decisions 2009/371/JPA, 2009/935/JHA and 2009/10/939 as well as Commission Implementing Decisions of 1 October 2009/968/JTA, 1 October 2010/934/JMA and 1 October 2011/937 as regards the appointment and removal of the Chief Data Protection Officer (CPO) and the Chief Information Officer (DPO).
For more information, see:
European Data Privacy Supervisor (European Data protection supervisor) (European Commission).

Summary 70:
EU’s own resources — recycling of plastic packaging waste and recycling of waste from waste containers (OJ L 86, 12.3.2005, pp. 1-8)
EU‘s own resource system
SUMMARY OF:
Decision (EU) 2020/852 — EU system of own resources
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?
It establishes a system of EU own resources.
It aims to ensure that the European Union (EU), in order to meet its financial needs, has sufficient resources to cover its liabilities resulting from the exceptional and temporary empowerment to borrow funds.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The decision sets out the total amount of its own resources that the Commission may annually call from a Member State. It does not exceed 1.40 % of the sum of all the Member States’ gross national income (GNI).
The own resources must be collected by Member States in accordance with the national provisions imposed by law, regulation or administrative action.
The Commission may only call for own resources from Member States when it considers that they are necessary to cover the costs of the EU’'s financial needs. The own resources may not exceed €1.4 billion for each Member State and €2.8 billion for the EU as a whole.
Collection costs
Member States may retain, by way of collection costs, 25% of the amounts referred to in point (a) of Article 2(1) of the decision.
A uniform call rate of €0.80 per kilogram is applied to the weight of packaging waste generated in each year that is not recycled.
the amount of waste collected must correspond to 3.8 kilograms multiplied by the population of the Member State in which the waste is generated.
In addition, Member States must ensure that their own resources do not exceed the amount of GNI collected by the Commission.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to improve the efficiency and transparency of the own resources system. These include:
the establishment of a database of Member States' own resources;
the introduction of a uniform call-rate to be applied to waste generated from plastic packaging.
For more information, see:
‘The EU's own resources’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Own resources: the amount the Commission can call on Member States to cover their own payments.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision of 17 July 2020 on the establishment of the European System of Own Resources
