Summary 71:
Wet grip tyre labelling
Wet-grip tyres
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/1242 on the labelling of tyres
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to encourage end-users to purchase tyres with higher wet grip performance by providing them with harmonised information on the wet grip parameter.
KEY POINTS
The regulation sets out the rules for the display of a tyre label on tyres at the point of sale, as well as in technical promotional material, to ensure that distributors and potential consumers receive the relevant tyre parameters at the time and place of the purchasing decision.
Tyre suppliers are responsible for ensuring that the tyre label and the product information sheet on tyres are displayed in a way that is clear, legible and easily understood.
The tyre label must contain the following information:
the wet grip class;
the weight of the tyre;
a description of the tyres’ characteristics;
specific precautions, if any, that must be taken when the tyre type is assembled, installed, maintained or tested;
measures performed with the measured technical parameters.
Suppliers must ensure that tyre suppliers enter the information set out in Annex VII into the product database before placing on the market a tyre produced after 1 May 2021. This information must be entered into the database before any new tyres are placed on the European market.
Distributors must also ensure that tyres are labelled in a manner that is clearly visible to the end-user at the same time as the tyre information sheet and which has the same technical characteristics that are relevant to the label.
End-users must be able to read the information on tyres before making a purchasing decision, including the tyre class and the weight and weight of tyres.
Manufacturers and tyre importers must ensure the tyres they sell conform with the regulation’s technical specifications.
In addition, tyre suppliers must provide the European Commission with a product database containing information on all tyres on sale, including:
wet grip classes;
weight and weight;
internal rolling resistance;
wetting resistance (RRC).
The Commission may adopt delegated acts in accordance with Article 14 of the regulation to adapt the values, calculation methods and requirements set out therein to technological progress.
If a tyre manufacturer fails to comply with these delegated acts, it may be subject to a penalty.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?

Summary 72:
Integrated Border Management Fund (IBMF) for the purchase, maintenance and upgrading of customs control equipment (2027-2027)
IntegratedBorder Management Fund
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2021/444 — Integrated Border Management Instrument for the period from 1 January 2021 to 31 December 2027
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes an integrated border management fund (‘the IBMF’).
It aims to support the European Union’s external borders in order to improve the control of goods entering and exiting the EU and to ensure both safety and security.
KEY POINTS
Customs controls are to be understood not only as enforcement of customs legislation but also as the enforcement of other legislation governing the entry, exit, transit, movement, storage and end-use of goods moved between the customs territory of the Union and countries or territories outside the EU, and the presence and movement within the EU of non-EU goods and goods placed under the end-using procedure.
The IBMF supports the implementation of the EU customs code and the customs programme for cooperation in the field of customs (the ‘Customs programme’), which establishes the customs union and customs authorities. The IBMF is designed to ensure the optimal use of financial resources in achieving the objectives of the Customs Code and the EU Customs programme.
Implementation and forms of EU funding
The EU funding for the IBMF has been divided into 2 categories:
EU funding for procurement for the procurement of equipment;
EU financing for the equipment for testing new pieces of equipment or new functionalities for existing items of equipment in operational conditions.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLACE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 29 July 2021.
BACKGROUND
The IMF is the first integrated border-management fund established by the European Parliament and the Council. It covers the procurement, maintenance, testing, evaluation and evaluation of equipment at the EU external borders.
For more information, see:
Border management fund
External borders (European Commission).

Summary 73:
Information unbundling of the electricity market
Information unbunification of the energy market
SUMMARY OF:
Directive (EU) 2019/943 on information-bundling rules applicable to transmission system operators
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DIRECTIVE?
It lays down rules on the unbundlement of the European Union’s electricity market.
It recasts and repeals Directive 2012/27/EU.
KEY POINTS
Transmission system operators (TSOs) are required to:
ensure that the information they provide to the European Commission and the European Energy Agency (EAA) on their electricity network is made available to all consumers;
provide the Commission with all relevant information on their network and their energy consumption;
take all necessary measures to ensure that the transmission system owner and the remaining part of the undertaking do not use joint services, such as joint legal services, apart from purely administrative or IT functions.
The transmission system operator must supply the Commission, the EAA or the European Network of Transmission System Operators for Electricity (ENTSO for Electricity) with all the necessary information on its network and its energy consumption. This information must be made available in all cases when access for recharging points has been denied. It must also be available to the Commission and to the public in the form of a price breakdown of electricity bills.
EU countries must ensure that:
the information they make available to consumers is transparent, non-discriminatory and market-based;
they make it publicly available;
transparency and non-discrimination-free;
it is made publicly available in accordance with the principles laid down in Annex II of the directive.
the Commission may impose effective, proportionate and dissuasive penalties on those entities where they do not comply with their obligations.
Regulatory authorities have the power to refuse to certify or designate an independent system operator if they believe that they are not complying with the rules.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS DIRECTIVE APPLY?
The directive entered into force on 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to modernise and modernise the European electricity market, including:
re-energising and modernising the electricity network;
improving the efficiency of energy networks;
ensuring the transparency and security of energy infrastructure;
establishing a single market for energy storage facilities.
For more information, see:
‘Unbundled electricity market’ on the Commission's website.

Act

Summary 74:
European High Performance Computing Joint Undertaking (EHPCJoint Undertaking) (until 31 December 2033) — vision for a common European vision in high-performance computing and quantum computing
European High-Performance Computing Joint undertaking (EHPCJ)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2016 establishing the European High Performance Computation Joint Undergoing
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a joint undertaking to promote the European Union’s (EU) vision in the field of high performance computing (HPC) and the development and uptake of quantum computing technologies, systems and applications.
It sets out the tasks of the Governing Board and the Executive Director.
KEY POINTS
The European High-Performing Computing Joint undertaking aims to:
establish a federated and interconnected supercomputing and data infrastructure and its services, as well as for training facilities and skills development opportunities;
promote the use of supercomputers and quantum simulators;
provide and manage access to a high-end supercomputer and quantum simulation infrastructure;
ensure the security of the supply chain;
contribute to the research and development of high-performing computing technologies and systems.
Objectives
The objective of the joint undertaking is to establish in Europe a Pursuing a common strategic Union vision in HPC and to ensure a leading role in the digital economy. This vision includes:
promoting the adoption of HPC technologies;
encouraging the development of new technologies; and systems;
supporting the research, development and deployment of advanced computing technologies.
providing and managing access to the infrastructure and services.
The Governing board is composed of representatives of the participating EU countries. It is chaired by the European Commission and consists of representatives from each participating EU country and representatives from the private sector.
Functioning
The governing board is responsible for:
the management of the Joint undertaking;
the coordination of the work programme;
setting priorities;
identifying priorities and identifying priorities.
Management of contributions from the participating countries.
Acquisition and ownership of the supercomputer infrastructure
The hosting entity is selected by the governing board following a call for expression of interest evaluated by independent experts. The hosting entity must be established in accordance with the terms and conditions set out in the regulation. The remaining total cost of ownership is covered by the hosting entity or by the Participating States in the hosting consortium, possibly supplemented by the contributions referred to in Article 6.
Implementation of the project
The project is implemented through European Partnerships, with private and/or public sector partners, in order to achieve the greatest possible impact of EU funding and the most effective contribution to the EU's policy objectives.
Joint undertaking
The Joint undertaking is governed by a governing board comprising representatives of participating countries and representatives of private sector partners. It has the following powers:
to:
make decisions on the organisation and operation of the Joint undertaking, including appointing its Executive Director;
make recommendations and recommendations on the implementation of its mission and objectives;
draw up and implement its work programme.
In addition, it has the power to appoint and terminate contracts for the provision of services and the management of its infrastructure.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
The regulation entered into force on 31 December 2016.
BACKGROUND
The EHPC Joint undertaking was established under the framework of the Digital Europe programme under Article 187 of the Treaty on the Functioning of the EU.
For more information, see:
‘European High performance computing’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* High-performant computing: a supercomputer or a system capable of performing high-precision calculations.
* Quantum simulation: a system consisting of a quantum computer or a quantum simulator.

Summary 75:
Climate-neutrality objective: 2030-2050 EU climate policy
Climate - neutrality objective
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 401/2009 on climate neutrality
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the objective for the EU’s climate policy to be ‘climate-neutral’.
It aims to ensure that all relevant EU legislation and policies are consistent with, and contribute to, the fulfilment of the climate-neutral objective while respecting a level playing field.
KEY POINTS
The objective is based on the principles of the Paris Agreement adopted under the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change (the ‘Paris Agreement’), guided by its principles and on the basis of the best available scientific knowledge, in the context of the long-term temperature goal.
The EU is committed to stepping up efforts to tackle climate change and to delivering on the implementation of the agreement adopted in December 2015.
To achieve this objective, the EU must reduce greenhouse gas emissions and removals (GHG emissions) in line with its 2030 climate target. This objective should be achieved by:
reducing GHG emissions and removing them from the EU economy;
ensuring a low-carbon economy by 2020;
contributing to the sustainable development of the environment;
recovering biodiversity;
adapting to climate change.
Climate neutrality
The regulation sets out a number of objectives, including:
climate neutrality: the objective to reduce GHGigaton emissions to a minimum of 0.5% of the total GHGCO2 emissions by 2030;
by 2040;
the objective to be reduced to 0.
carbon dioxide emissions by 20% of total GHGs by 2040.
In order to achieve the climate neutrality objective, EU legislation must:
be consistent with the Paris agreement and its objectives;
take account of the advice of the Advisory Board set up under Regulation (EU) 2021/2040 on climate policy;
be based on best available science and based on an indicative, linear trajectory linking the EU greenhouse gas budget for the 2030 to 2050 period.
National climate advisory bodies can play an important role in, and advise the Commission on, the development of EU climate policies. The Advisory Board is composed of representatives of the EU countries and experts from the private sector. It advises the Commission and the European Parliament and the Council of the European Union on how to implement the EU 2030 climate policy. It also provides guidance on the EU ETS.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The Paris Agreement on climate change was signed in Paris on 12 December 2015 and the EU has committed itself to taking action to meet its objectives.
For more information, see:
‘Climate neutrality’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Carbon dioxide emissions: the total amount of greenhouse gases emitted from the burning of fossil fuels by the human body. This includes all greenhouse gases that are emitted into the atmosphere, including those from power plants, industrial plants and nuclear power plants.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егандрарска гакацка   бакова  вакта
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) 2019/852 of 12 December 2019 on the objective of climate neutrality (OJ L 157, 14.12.2019, pp. 1-8)

’.

Implementation and forms of EU funding

In exceptional cases, during a health crisis caused by a serious cross-border threat to health, costs incurred by entities established in non-associated countries may be considered eligible if those costs are duly justified for reasons concerning countering the spreading of the risk for the protection of health of the citizens in the Union.
The Commission is responsible for implementing the programme. The power to adopt delegated acts is conferred on the Commission subject to certain conditions, including those relevant to the Union agencies, including through their common communication and through the EU4Health steering group.

Summary 77:
Cultural and audiovisual strand of the European Union’s 2019/2020 programme (Cultural strand)
Culture strand of European Union's 2019/2021 programme (SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2019/790 — European Union programme for the promotion of European culture and media
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the implementation of the ‘European Union Programme for the Promotion of European Culture and Media’ (CULTURE strand).
It aims to promote the European cultural and media sectors in the new digital environment, including through innovative business models.
It also aims to stimulate interest in, and improve access to, European cultural works, including heritage works, and to support the engagement and development of audiences of all ages, in particular young audiences, across Europe and beyond.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The programme covers the following sectors:
cinema and audi-visual media (e.g. film, television, radio, digital media, etc.);
culture and media (film, TV, radio and digital media);
the European heritage label (the ‘Heritage Label’), the European Heritage Days, the European prizes in the areas of contemporary, rock and pop music, literature, heritage and architecture and the European Capitals of Culture;
the promotion of young audiences;
publication of European films and television programmes;
audi-related initiatives.
The European Commission is responsible for the management of the programme. It also manages the annual work programmes.
Programme priorities
Cultures strand
Cinema strand
The Culture strand is composed of the following priorities:
promoting European cinema and television;
encouraging interest in and improving access to European cinema;
supporting young audiences in and through the creation and distribution of European film and television content;
providing technical and administrative support to the European Audiovisuality Observatory.
Audi-Visual media strand
In addition to promoting European cinema, the Visual Media strand aims to:
encourage the creation of, distribution of and access to new European films;
promote young audiences and young people in the European cinema sector;
ensure that European films are made available to all audiences, including young people;
increase the visibility and visibility of European cinema in the digital environment;
raise awareness of the importance of the role of the visual media sector in European society and in the development of European cultural policies;
contribute to the creation, distribution and access of European works in the context of the digitalisation of the EU;
improve the visibility of the work of the Observatory and the quality of the information it provides to the public on European cinema.
Publication and dissemination of European media
The Commission publishes an annual report on the activities of the Culture strand. The report covers the priorities set out in Articles 5, 6 and 7 and the descriptions of the actions that are eligible for funding under the programme, as well as the objectives of the activities that are not eligible under the Programme. The Commission also publishes a list of the beneficiaries of the funding.
EU funding and methods of implementation
The Programme is managed by the European Commission under the auspices of the Directorate-General for the Internal Market, which is assisted by the Agency for Research, Innovation and Entrepreneurship (RIA) and the Directorate General for the European External Action Service. The European Commission manages the programme and manages the budget. It receives proposals from the public and the private sectors for actions under its management. It assesses these proposals and evaluates them according to the criteria laid down in Annex I of the Regulation. It then decides on the actions to be funded under the CULTURE programme.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2019.
BACKGROUND
The Rome Declaration of 25 March 2017 and the EU Council of 14 and 15 December 2017 stated that education and culture are key to building inclusive and cohesive societies for all and to sustaining European competitiveness.
Cultural policies have directly reached millions of European citizens, have demonstrated the social and economic benefits of European policies, and should therefore be continued and whenever possible expanded.
For more information, see:
‘Culture and media’ on the Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Cinema: the production, distribution, promotion, and consumption of European artistic and creative works. It includes films, television programmes, radio programmes, and the internet.

contribute to tackling global and societal challenges, including the SDGs by following the principles of the Paris Agreement adopted under the United Nations Framework Convention on Climate Change, and to achieving a net-zero greenhouse gas economy by 2050 at the latest;
improve the quality of research and innovation in the European Union (EU);
promote cooperation between universities and research institutes (KICs) in the field of innovation;
encourage innovation ecosystems and relevant actors of the knowledge triangle.
To achieve this, the EIT:
encourages cooperation between KICs, universities and universities;
provides financial support for research, innovation and innovation activities;
contributes to tackling climate change and the sustainable management of water-marine ecosystems;
supports the development of smart specialisation platforms (SSPP);
contains a multiannual strategy, which aims to improve the management of marine ecosystems.
promotes the exchange of good practices and learning between universities, universities, colleges and universities.
The strategic objectives of the strategy are based on the following:
the creation of an EU-wide network of innovation ecosystems (i.e. networks of universities and colleges in the fields of innovation, research and technology;
improving the quality and dissemination of good practice and learning resulting from the activities of universities, institutes and colleges of higher education and research;
promoting the integration of new partners that add value to the European Innovation Networks (e.g. universities, research institutions and universities);
enhancing the knowledge-based economy of the EU;
creating a European Innovation Network (EINN).
The strategy is based on a number of measures that aim to adapt and improve the current functioning of EIT and the KIC. These include:
increasing the visibility of the EINN and its activities in the context of the 2020–2030 period;
increasing its capacity to generate best innovation added-value.
In addition, the strategy sets out:
a number of key actions, including:
research and innovation (RIS) activities, which are designed to promote and facilitate the integration and integration of potential new partners;
the development of innovative products and services;
exchange of best practice and good practices;
research on water management management (WMM);
the promotion of water management;
environmental issues;
science and technology for sustainable development.
EIT also aims to promote the collaboration between relevant universities, institutions and research centres in the area of innovation.
RIS activities
The aim of RIS activities is to promote:
exchanges of best practices and good practice;
participation of universities in RIS activities; and
promotion of the participation of the public and private sectors in RIS.
A number of initiatives are also planned for RIS activities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
The regulation applies from 1 January 2021.
BACKGROUND
The European Institute is one of the most innovative institutes in the EU. It is funded by the Cohesion Policy Funds and other EU, national and regional programmes.
For more information, see:
‘European Institute’ on the European Commission's website.

Summary 79:
Aromatised wine products — rules on the definition, description, presentation, labelling and protection of geographical indications of certain aromatised wines (Regulation (EU) No 1169/2011)
Aromated wine products – rules on definitions, presentation and labelling
SUMMARY OF:
Implementing Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1201/2012 on the rules applicable to the definition and description of certain aromatic-based wine products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and restrictions on aromatisation* of certain wine products.
It aims to ensure that consumers’ expectations as regards quality and production methods are met, while taking into account traditional production methods.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
wine products produced in accordance with the rules laid down in Article 2(2)(o) of Regulation (EC) No 882/2004 on the protection of the geographical indications* of wine products;
sugars and spirit-based wines with an alcoholic strength by volume of not less than 17.5 % vol. and a total alcoholic strength of not more than 17% vol.
Sales denominations
The European Commission may supplement the sales denominations laid down by the regulation with the customary name of the product within the meaning of the regulation.
The Commission may adopt delegated acts in order to establish the conditions under which product specifications may include additional requirements to those referred to in Article 10(2) of this regulation regarding:
the information to be provided in the product specification with regard to the link between the geographical area and the final product;
the means of making the decisions on protection or rejection of the names of the products;the submission of trans-border applications;the checks and verification to be carried out by the Member States, including testing.
Existing geographical designations
The geographical indications listed in the regulation are protected in its country of origin. However, they may be supplemented by a customary name in exceptional cases. The Commission must make their names and addresses public and update them periodically.
Protection of producers’ names
A producer name protected under this regulation must be registered with the European Commission. It must be protected with due regard for local and traditional usage and for any risk of confusion.
In exceptional cases, a single producer name in question may be protected in more than one Member State, provided that the name partially homonymous with that of a name already registered under the regulation does not mislead the consumer into believing that products come from another territory.
Labelling and presentation
The product specification must be published in a single document in the Official Journal of the European Union (OJ) with the following information:
a description of the characteristics of the wine and its production methods
the quantity and quality of the wines and their alcoholic strength
the number of units sold per hectolitre of wine and/or spirit and the number of hectolitres of spirit;
an indication of the quantity of wine-based spirits and the percentage of spirits and spirits of spirit in the wine category.

WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION?

promote sustainable development and poverty reduction;

Summary 82:
Management, conservation and control measures for Mediterranean swordfish
Mining, fishing and fishing gear — management, conservation, technical and scientific measures for the conservation of Atlantic Tunas
Management and conservation measures applicable in the Convention area of the International Commission for the Conservation of Mediterranean Swordfish
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EU) 2017/2107 laying down management, scientific and technical measures for managing, conserving and controlling the management and control of the conservation and management of the marine environment in the area covered by the Convention Area of the ICCAT Convention
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the rules and general principles concerning mechanisms for control by Member States of the European Commission’s exercise of implementing powers under the Convention on the Conservation and Management of the Marine Tunas (ICCAT Convention).
KEY POINTS
Management measures
Member States must:
ensure that vessels fishing for, retained on board, transhipped, transported, transported or landed in the context of recreational fisheries do not use harpoons or pelagic longlines;
monitor the fishing effort of vessels engaged in recreational fishing.
Monitoring and surveillance
Vessel monitoring and surveillance systems must be in place to:
monitor vessels’ movements and movements;
assess the number of vessels flying their flag flying the flag that fished for, retain on board or transshipped, transship, transported and landed swordfish;
keep a record of the quantity of swordfish caught, retained and landed;
check the catch and the geographical area where the catch was taken;
report to the Commission every year.
The Commission must send that information to ICCAT Secretariat by 30 April, 30 July and 30 October of each year and by 30 January of the following the following year and send it to the European Parliament, the Council and the European Economic and Social Committee (EEC) by 30 June of the same year. This information must include:
the name of the vessel, where applicable;
vessel's length overall;
name and address of owner(s) and operator(s);
the information on the catch;
the catch data, including length (LJFL) and live weight (live weight) of each swordfish.
Each Member State must inform the Commission without delay when the uptake of the quota for swordfish allocated to a fishing gear type is deemed to have reached 80 %. The Commission must then inform the European Maritime Safety Agency (EMSA) and the EEC of the measures taken to ensure that the quota is not exceeded.
EU countries must submit electronically to the ESEA every year the following information:
time of arrival;
number of vessels;
estimated quantity of fish caught;
recovered swordfish retained;
catch data;
location of the catch.
An annual report must be sent to the ECSA by 31 January each year. The report must contain:
details of the number and type of vessels registered in the Member State;
results of inspections carried out during the preceding year;
measures taken to prevent, reduce or eliminate infringements;
information on vessels authorised to target swordfish using harpoons (including the number, type and duration of harpoons used);
reciprocal measures taken by the Member States to prevent or reduce infringements.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 15 November 2017.
BACKGROUND
The EU is a party to the International Convention for Conservation of the Mediterranean Tunas Convention (‘the ICCAT convention’). The scope of that convention includes vessels engaging in recreational fisheries.
For more information, see:
Fishing effort and management (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Delegated Regulations (EC) No 1224/2009 of 15 November 2009 laying down the management, technological and scientific rules for the Convention Areas of the ICT Convention and amending Council Regulations (EU, Euratom) No 1936/2001, (EC, No 1342/2008 and (EC), No 520/2007 (OJ L 315, 30.11.2009, pp. 1-8)

Summary 84:
Environmental and climate objectives of the European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMFF)
Environmental and Climate objectives of The European Maritime & Fisheries Fund
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2021/1060 laying down the priorities and specific rules for providing EU funding to the European Marine and Fisheries Facility
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the EMFF’s priorities, its budget and the specific rules that apply to it.
The EMFF is a key enabler for sustainable fisheries and the conservation of marine biological resources, for food security through the supply of seafood products, for the growth of a sustainable blue economy and for healthy, safe, secure, clean and sustainably managed seas and oceans.
KEY POINTS
Objectives
The objective of the EMFAF is to:
ensure sustainable fisheries;
conserve aquatic biological resources;
improve the environmental and climate status of the oceans;
contribute to the sustainable development of the blue economy;
promote the sustainable management of marine ecosystems;
encourage the sustainable use of marine resources.
Specific objectives
The objectives are:
fisheries;
aquaculture;
environmental and climate policy;
clean and sustainable marine ecosystems.
Funding
EU funding is based on a number of criteria, including:
the objective of sustainable fishing;
the specific objective of protecting the marine environment; and
the objectives of sustainable aquaculture.
In addition, support may be granted for the joint first acquisition of a fishing vessel by several natural persons who each fulfil the conditions set out in Article 14 of the regulation.
Support may also be provided for:
permanent cessation of fishing activities;
fishing vessels that are no longer used for commercial purposes;
equipment that is being repaired or replaced;
more fuel than the engine being replaced under the normal fishing effort of the vessel concerned.
Evaluation
The European Commission must:
assess the results of EMFF programmes and operations;
monitor and evaluate the results;
take appropriate measures to prevent, reduce or eliminate serious non-compliance with the rules of the CFP by the Member State;
make recommendations to the Member States on how to improve the environmental status of their oceans and seas;
provide information and communication actions to the public on the implementation of these measures.
Budget
The regulation sets out a budget for the 2018-2020 programming period. The EMFF has a budget of €2.5 billion.
EU countries may apply a flat rate or extrapolated financial correction in accordance with the criteria for applying flat rates.
Monitoring and evaluation
The Commission:
reports to the Council and the European Parliament on the financial rules applicable to EMFF;
conducts regular monitoring and evaluation activities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 18 July 2018.
BACKGROUND
The EU has committed to eliminating subsidies contributing to fisheries overcapacity and overfishing.
For more information, see:
Fisheries and the oceans (European Commission).

Summary 85:
Convention on the Conservation and Management of Straddling Fish and Highly Migratory Fish Stocks (C-MSTS)
Convention of the United Nations Convention on the conservation and management of straddling fish and highly migratory fish stocks (C)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2005 on the Convention relating to the Conservation of Stradling Fish Stock and HighlyMigratory Fishes Stocks and the Agreement for the Implementation of that Convention relating thereto
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the Convention is fully implemented.
It applies to EU fishing vessels used or intended for use for the purposes of fishing in the area covered under the Convention.
KEY POINTS
The Convention covers:
the area between 96° and 110°W and between 4°N and 3°S;
the areas of the Indian Ocean and the Pacific Ocean;
fishing on data buoys in the Convention area.
EU countries must:
ensure that vessels do not interact with these buoys;
keep records of the number of discards and releases of Mobulid rays, the status (dead or alive) of sharks and the carcasses of oceanic whitetip sharks (Carcharhinus longimanus);
keep a register of vessels that have been in breach of the Convention’s rules.
The IATTC is to have an integral role in coordinating the implementation of the Agreement and in implementing the measures that will be adopted within the framework of the convention.
Observers must fulfil the qualification criteria set out in the Annex II to the Agreement.
Fishing vessels must promptly release sharks (whether alive or dead) caught that are not retained unharmed, to the extent practicable, as soon as they are seen in the net or on the deck, without compromising the safety of any persons.
Purse seine fishing vessels must also:
not be towed out of a purse seine net;
not retain onboard, tranship, land, store, sell or offer for sale any part or whole carcass of sharks;
be notified of any sealed wells on-board the vessel that are opened and when it is resealed.
Regional vessel register
The European Union must: ensure that vessels are registered in the I-T-T system;
provide the Commission with a copy of the observer report on alleged incidents involving assault or harassment of the observers upon request.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATED APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
 
  The Convention on Straddled Fish and High Migrated Fishes is one of the most important conservation agreements in the world. It was adopted in 1982.
For more information, see:
Conservation and Management (European Commission).

Summary 86:
Common Understanding on delegated acts and on the related standard clauses of the Lisbon Treaty (Joint Political Declaration of 27 October 2011 on the Common Understanding on Delegated Acts and the related Standard Clauses of the European Parliament, the Council and the Commission on explanatory documents (Common Understanding)
Common Decision (EU) 2016/852 on the conclusion of the Joint Political Declaration on the common understanding on delegated and implementing acts
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE AGREEMENT AND THE DECISION?
The agreement establishes a common framework for the implementation of delegated or implementing acts in the European Union (EU).
The decision concludes the agreement on behalf of the EU.
KEY POINTS
Delegated acts
The three institutions recognise the need for the alignment of all existing legislation to the legal framework introduced by the Lisbon treaty, and the need to give high priority to delegated acts, within the limits of the Treaties. The three institutions have agreed on a Common Understanding (COUNCIL) on delegated laws and on implementing acts. The agreement sets out common objectives and tasks for the following year.
The aim of the agreement is to:
improve the efficiency and effectiveness of the legislative process;
ensure that delegated acts are implemented effectively and efficiently;
improve cooperation between the three institutions;
encourage the participation of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and other end-users in the decision-making process.
In addition, the agreement also sets out a number of tools for better law-making, such as:
implementation of delegated acts;
ex-post evaluation of existing legislation;
the use of the recasting technique;
transposition of directives in the EU’s’ legal framework.
exchange of information between the institutions.
Joint declaration
The joint declaration sets out broad objectives and priorities for the next year and will identify items of major political importance which, without prejudice to the powers conferred on the co-legislators, should receive priority treatment in legislative process. It will also identify areas of cooperation and information-sharing between the bodies concerned.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE

Summary 87:
Citizens’ initiative registration — EU rules for online data collection
Citizens' initiative registration – EU rules on online data collecting
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2013 on the registration of citizens’ initiatives
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European Union (EU) online data-collection system for citizens‘ initiatives.
It aims to facilitate the exchange of information between the European Commission and the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee (EEASC) and the Commission itself.
KEY POINTS
Organisers of citizens' initiatives
Organisations must:
register a citizens' initiative with the Commission;
collect the necessary statements of support from signatories in paper or electronic form;
certify that the organisers have complied with the regulation’s requirements;
use the information they have collected in processing personal data pursuant to this regulation.
The organisers must: meet the minimum number of signatories required in each EU country, multiplied by 750;provide the Commission with a proposal inviting it to submit a proposal for a legal act of the Union for the purpose of implementing the Treaties similar to the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union, and on the Council under Article 241 TFEU.
They must ensure that:
the organisers are citizens of the EU and are of the age to be entitled to vote for the preparation of the initiative and its submission to the Commission.
If the organisers fail to comply with the requirements, they must be subject to appropriate penalties for infringements of this regulation and in particular for:
false declarations made by organisers;
the fraudulent use of data.
Registration procedure
The Commission:
submits a request inviting the Commission to publish a proposal on the website of an initiative;
publishes a list of the signatories, including the date, signature and official stamp of the competent authority;
ensures that the Commission receives a copy of the request within 3 months of receiving it;
assesses the quality of the information it has received and publishes it in a publicly accessible format;
establishes a register of the signed statements.
In addition, the Commission must ensure:
that the organisers:
have the necessary information to carry out the registration procedure;
make available an open-source software for the purposes of the registration;
verify and certify the organisers’ statements;
keep copies of the statements for at least 1 year.
Notification of national provisions
Each EU country must notify the Commission the specific provisions it adopts in order to implement this Regulation. The Commission must inform the other EU countries of these provisions.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The regulation entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
Citizen's initiative registration (CIR)
CIR is a procedure that allows citizens to directly approach the Commission for a legislative act. It allows them to express their views on a proposed EU legal act.
For more information, see:
Cir (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Citizens’ Initiative: a proposal to implement a Treaty, Treaty or Council Act.
* Legal act: a legal instrument adopted by an EU Member State to implement the Treaty of Lisbon, Treaty of Rome or Treaty of Amsterdam.
ACT
Commission Regulation (EC), No 553/2013 of 21 December 2013 on the Registration of Citizens' Initiatives and amending the Annexes to the Regulation.

Summary 88:
Sustainable use of pesticides: EU statistics on the use of agricultural pesticides (Eurostat Regulation)
Sustainable application of pesticides — Eurostat Regulation
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1107/2009 on the sustainable use of pesticide statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out EU-wide rules on the statistical collection, transmission and processing of statistics on pesticides.
It aims to ensure that the EU’s statistical programme committee, established by Council Decision 89/382/EEC, Euratom, is consulted on the implementation of this regulation.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
pesticides used on agricultural crops;
the production, storage and distribution of pesticides;
use of pesticides on non-target crops.
EU countries must compile statistics on pesticide use for each selected crop within a reference period as defined in the annexes to the regulation. These statistics must be sent to the European Commission, Eurostat and the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA).
The Commission must assess the quality of the data transmitted and transmit them to the EFSA.
Data collection and transmission
Eurostat must collect, transmit and transmit data on the pesticide use of each crop within the reference period defined in Annex II of the regulation, as well as on the number of pesticides used on each crop. The data must be presented in accordance with the classification given in Annex III.
The European Union (EU) Member States must send Eurostat a report on the data collected and transmitted to the Commission every 2 years. The report must include:
the total number of pesticide applications for each crop;
a description of the pesticides used and the number and types of pesticides applied;
an indication of the number, types and categories of pesticides covered by the regulation;
data on the total pesticides applied and the types and quantities applied.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
  
It has applied since 24 November 2009 and had to become law in the Member States by 24 November 2011.
BACKGROUND
The EU has adopted a number of measures to reduce the risks associated with pesticide use, including:
Directive 2009/43/EC — the EU strategy on sustainable uses of pesticides (see summary);
Regulations (EC, EFSA, EEA, EEC and Euratom — the Sustainable Use of Pesticides — see summary.
For more information, see:
Pesticides (European Commission).

Summary 89:
Plant protection products — EU rules on active substances and active substances (Regulation (EC) No 552/2007)
Plant Protection Products — EU Rules on Active Substances
SUMMARY OF:
Commission Regulation (EU) No 529/2007 on the application for authorisation of plant protection products
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the granting of EU-wide authorisations to substances* for the protection of plants, parts of plants or plant products against harmful organisms.
It aims to ensure that EU countries apply the same criteria when granting authorisations for plant protection* products.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to substances, including micro-organisms having general or specific action against harmful bacteria, viruses or fungi, as well as to plants, part of plants and plant products, referred to as ‘active substances’. It does not apply to substances that are not active substances.
Authorisations are granted on the basis of the following criteria:
the substances must be safe for human and animal health and the environment;
the plant protection product must not pose a risk to human, animal or plant health and environmental conditions relevant to the use of the product in question and representative of the conditions prevailing in the zone where the product is intended to be used.
The European Commission may, in exceptional cases, apply the comparative assessment when granting an authorisation.
EU countries must compile a file on each application. The applicant must submit a dossier containing:
a description of the active substance, safener or synergist;
a list of test and study reports on the product’s safety and environmental performance;
an application for the authorisation holder.
the applicant must provide samples and analytical standards.
An EU country may withdraw or amend its measure if it concludes that the objectives of Article 4(1)(a)(iv) and (b) of Directive 2001/18/EC on the deliberate release into the environment of genetically modified organisms may not be achieved.
If an EU country considers that an active substance or a synergist does not meet the criteria, it withdraws or changes its measure.
Reporting and exchange of information
The Commission must report to the European Food Safety Authority (EFSA) and the European Parliament and the Council of the information it receives from EU countries on applications for authorisations. The Commission may set a time limit within which the information must be transmitted.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
 
It has applied since 1 January 2008.
BACKGROUND
  * KEY TERMS
* Active substance: a substance having general, specific or specific effect against harmful micro-organism or on plants, plants or plants parts.
* Safener: an agent that reduces the risk of the presence of a substance in a plant or plant product.
Combination: a process whereby two or more substances combine to form a single substance, such as a solvents, to reduce the risk to the environment.
Safer: a compound that reduces, reduces or eliminates a substance that is likely to be harmful to human or animal health, the environment or plants.
Active substances: substances that have the ability to prevent, neutralise or neutralise a substance from being absorbed into the soil, plant matter or plant material.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, Euratom of 21 December 2007 establishing a European Union system for the approval of active substances, amending Council Directive 91/414/EEC with any necessary modifications.
Successive amendments and corrections to Council Regulation (Euratom) No 555/2007 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

See consolidated version.

Summary 90:
SOLVIT: Information exchange network (IMI)
SolveIT:Information exchange network
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 182/2011 on the establishment of the Information Exchange Network (IMI)
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European Union (EU) system for the exchange of information between EU countries and the European Commission.
It sets out the rules and general principles concerning the use of IMI.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
the EU’s internal market area for which IMI is to be used;
the internal market areas for which the Commission is competent.
EU countries may appoint one or more IMI coordinators in order to carry out any of the tasks listed in the regulation, in accordance with its internal administrative structure. These coordinators are assisted by a committee composed of representatives of the EU countries.
The Commission may play a consultative role in that process.
Information exchange with non-EU countries
The European Commission is responsible for:
exchanging information between IMI users in the EU;
providing technical assistance to the IMI coordinator;
ensuring that the information exchanged in IMI complies with the rights of data subjects;
assisting the national coordinator in the management of the SOLVIT network.
Rights of users and data subjects
The rights of users are set out in the annex to the regulation. They include:
access rights to their personal data;
protection of their privacy and security;
access to their data processing activities performed by an IMI user under their authority and to their rights as data subjects in cooperation with the Commission;
information to data subjects and transparency.
Each competent authority must be a controller with respect to its own data processing operations performed by a user under its authority and must ensure that data subjects can exercise their rights in compliance with Chapters III and IV, where necessary.
Processing of special categories of data
The IMI system allows for the processing of certain types of data, such as:
medical information;
financial information; and
personal data.
In addition, the European Data Protection Supervisor (EDPS) can:
ensure that personal data are processed only with the consent of the data subject, unless processing is requested for overriding reasons in the public interest;
act as an interlocutor of the Commission in the implementation of EU data protection acts.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 16 February 2011.
BACKGROUND
   
The EU has adopted a number of measures to improve the protection of personal data. Among them are:
Directive 95/46/EC on the sharing of information and establishing a European information exchange network;
Regulations (EC, Euratom) No 45/2001 and (EU), which set up the European Information Exchange System (EISA).
For more information, see:
‘Information Exchange Network’ on the European Agency for Safety and Health at Work’ website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Еганска бактарка
Council Regulation (EC), No 181/2011 of 15 February 2011 establishing the information exchange system (IMA) and amending Council Regulation (EEC), Euratom and Commission Implementing Implementing Regulations (EC and Euratom).
Successive amendments and corrections to the Regulation have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 91:
Fishing in the Mediterranean and Black Sea: rules on fishing, retention on board, transhipment and landing of fish and shellfish caught by vessels of more than 15 metres in overall length (GFCM Agreement area)
Fishing on board and in the Black Sea
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009 on the European Union’s system to prevent, deter and eliminate illegal, unreported and unregulated fishing
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules on the EU system of preventing, deterring and eliminating illegal, re-fishing of fish, shellfish and molluscs caught in the GFCM agreement area.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies from 1 January 2010 to 14 August of each year.
It does not apply to:
fishing, retention of fish or shellfish on board;
transshipment or landing of these fish and shells;
fisheries using fish aggregating devices (FADs);
the use of fishing gear.
Authorisation
EU countries must take the necessary measures to prohibit fishing, retaining on board or transshipment of:
fish caught during the fishing season;
shellfish caught on board during the landing period;
common dolphinfish (Coryphaena hippurus) fisheries using FADs.
The European Commission must keep a register of authorised vessels.
Vessels of an overall length of less than 10 metres must be included in a list containing the name of the vessel and its EU fleet register number, which the EU country concerned must provide to the Commission.
Fisheries in the area covered by the regulation must comply with the following rules:
the minimum mesh size must be at least:
a square-meshed net of 3 metres;
a small-line with a maximum length of 12 metres; and
a longline with an engine less than 50 percent of their longline if they are less than 12 metres in length;
the number of engines and propellers must be in accordance with the conditions of the authorisations.
Member States must inform the Commission, the Member States in whose waters the research is carried out and the Scientific, Technical and Economic Committee for Fisheries of all catches from such fishing operations.
Reporting of statistical matrices
The Commission must submit to the European Parliament and the Council a report on the fishing activities carried out in the areas covered by this regulation every 2 years. This report must include:
date, time, zone and place current fishing trip commenced;
areas visited (entry and exit from different areas);
transhipment, retention and landing results of the fishing operations;
records and documents (transport records and documents) of the fish in the hold or during landing.
Monitoring and reporting
The Member States must ensure that:
all fishing vessels registered in their territory are registered in the EU fleet registers;
there is a list of vessels that are not on the register;
authorised vessels are inspected at least once a year;
any vessel that enters or transits a port without prior authorisation must be inspected in all cases.
Before 1 February each year, Member States submit a report in electronic format a report to the EU Commission in electronic form on fishing activities. The report must contain:
dates and times of fishing trips commenced,
date and time of departure from the fishing area;
where applicable, the number of catches caught;
details of the number and type of engines, propellers and gear used.
Report
The report must be sent to the Council, the Commission and the scientific, technical and economic committee for fisheries of all the catches caught and transshipments from such operations. The Commission must also report to Member States on the number, type and number of vessels used for scientific investigations.

Summary 92:
Uniform patent protection within the internal market: European patent with unitary effect (EPC)
Uniform product patent protection: European product patent (EU)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1260/2012 implementing enhanced cooperation in the area of unitary patent protection with regard to the provisions of the European Patent Organisation
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European Patent with Unitary Effect*.
It aims to ensure that patent proprietors have the same legal protection in all EU countries.
It also establishes a Unified Patent Court to hear cases concerning the patent.
KEY POINTS
The European Patent Office (EPO) is the body responsible for the protection of patents in the European Union (EU).
The regulation applies to:
patents granted by the European patent proprietor in accordance with Articles 6(1) and 6(2) of the Treaty on Patent Cooperation (see summary);
patent applications submitted by patent owners in the EU countries;
the European patent granted by a patent owner in the Netherlands, Austria, Poland, Portugal, Romania, Slovenia, Slovakia, Finland, Sweden and the United Kingdom (‘participating EU countries’);
the patents granted by patent holders in the United States of America, Canada, France, Germany, Japan and Switzerland.
EU countries must ensure effective legal protection before a competent court of one or several participating EU countries against the decisions of the EPO in carrying out the tasks referred to in the regulation.
The EPO is responsible for:
the protection of patented inventions;
protecting intellectual property rights;
ensuring that patent owners have the right to use their inventions for commercial purposes;
assisting the European Commission in the implementation of the EPC’s rules on patents.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATED RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
From 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The EPC has been amended several times, most recently by the Agreement on Patent Court of the EU.
For more information, see:
European Patent Organisation (European Patent Office).
KEY TERMS
* European patent: a patent granting a patent to an object of property, i.e. an invention that has unitary effects.
* Object of property: an invention which has the legal effect of being a patent in its entirety and in all the countries where it is registered.
ACT
Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, of 17 December 2012 implementing enhanced Cooperation in the Area of Unitary Patent Protection (OJ L 157, 21.12.2012, pp. 1-8)
RELATED ACTS
Council Decision 2014/852/EU of 21 December 2014 on the signing, on behalf of the Commission, and provisional application of the agreement on patent court in the field of patent protection and repealing Council Regulation (EC) No 852/2013 (OJC) No 652/2014 (OCT) No 596/2013, and Council Decision 2013/853/EU on the conclusion of the Agreement between the Commission and the EU on patent protection.
Decision 2014/955/EU: on the provisional application by the Commission to the United Nations Patent Office of the Convention on the Protection of Intellectual Property Rights (COPR) and on the Protocol on Patent Protection of the International Patent Office.

Summary 93:
European Observatory on Counterfeiting and Piracy
European Observatory of Intellectual Property Rights
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 376/2014 on the European Observatory on Infringements of Intellectual property Rights
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up an EU-wide Observatory on counterfeiting and piracy.
It aims to provide reliable and comparable data on infringements of intellectual property rights.
KEY POINTS
The European Observatory (EOP) is a centre of excellence on information and data relating to intellectual property infringements. It is hosted and managed by the European Commission’s Directorate-General for the Internal Market and Competitiveness.
The EOP is composed of representatives from public administrations, bodies and organisations in the EU countries dealing with intellectual property and representatives from the private sector, for the purpose of their participation in its work.
In order to carry out its tasks, the EOP organises meetings at least once per year with representatives of the public administrations and bodies in EU countries, public and private sector representatives, as well as representatives of consumers and small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs).
It publishes a management report every 3 years on the results of its activities. It also publishes notices to the European Parliament, the Council, the Commission, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Administrative Board of the European Union (EASU).
In addition, it publishes an annual report on the work it has done.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULTRY APPLY?
The regulation has applied since 6 June 2014.
BACKGROUND
The Observatory was set up by Regulation (EC) No 207/2009 on the enforcement of copyright and trademarks.
For more information, see:

Summary 94:
Ensuring the effective exercise of the EU’s rights under international trade agreements (Trade in Services Regulation)
Ensuing the effectiveness of the Union's rights under International trade agreements
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 laying down the rules and general principles concerning mechanisms for control by the Member States of the European Commission's exercise of implementing powers
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules to ensure that the European Union is able to exercise its trade rights in the field of trade in services.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
public procurement;
trade in services;
international trade agreements.
It applies to the following:
the origin of a service;
the obligation on contracting authorities or entities conducting public procurement procedures to increase, subject to certain exceptions, the price of services and/or goods originating in certain third countries that have been offered in contract award procedures.
Public procurement
Each Member State must submit a list of appropriate contracting authorities* or entities* to the Commission for the purpose of determining the origin of the services or goods offered in public procurement. To provide the basis for this determination, each Member State shall submit a detailed list of relevant contracting authorities, entities or categories of contracting authorities and entities.
The Commission will consult the public authorities that may be involved in the implementation of possible commercial policy measures to be adopted by the EU. It will then report on its assessment to the European Parliament and the Council. The review may be followed up by appropriate legislative proposals.
Implementing measures
The European Commission may adopt implementing measures suspending concessions or other obligations in order to safeguard the EU's economic interests. These measures may be suspended, modified or repealed in accordance with the examination procedure referred to in Article 8(2) of the regulation. The Commission will submit a report to the Parliament and to the Council on its implementation of these measures. The Council will then adopt a decision on the basis of this report.
In the case of disputes arising between the EU and the other party or parties to an international trade agreement, the Commission will ensure that:
there is a positive solution to any disputes arising from the agreement;
there are no adverse economic impacts resulting from a third country measure;
any adverse economic impact resulting from the dispute is mitigated by the measures taken by the Commission.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It has applied since 16 February 2011.
BACKGROUND
International trade agreements are important tools for the EU to protect its economic interests, particularly in situations where non-EU countries enact trade restrictive measures that diminish the benefits accruing to the Union.
For more information, see:
International Trade Agreements (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 181/2011 of 15 February 2011 on the exercise of European Commission implementing powers pursuant to Articles 13 and 14 of the Trade in Services Regulations (OJ L 55, 28.2.2011, pp. 1-2)

Summary 95:
Bananas — EU-Central America agreement on the stabilisation mechanism for bananas (Regulation (EU) 2016/852)
Bananas – EU-Catchment Agreement
SUMMARY OF:
Delegated Regulation (EC) No 852/2012 on the implementation of the bilateral safeguard clause in the Agreement between the European Union and Central America on bananas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for implementing the agreement between the EU and the Central American countries of bananas.
It aims to prevent or remedy serious injury to the EU’s banana industry.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies only to products originating in the EU or in Central America. It does not apply to imports from non-EU countries.
Prior surveillance measures
In the event that there is an increase of imports concentrated in one or several of the EU's outermost regions or Member States, the Commission should be able to introduce prior surveillance measures. These measures must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
The Commission must:
impose provisional and definitive safeguard measures in the event of a threat of serious injury;
implement a prior surveillance procedure if there is sufficient prima facie evidence that imports of a product originating in a Central American country have increased as a result of the reduction or elimination of a customs duty in accordance with the Tariff Elimination Schedule, and that such imports cause serious injury, or threat thereof, to the Union industry;
suspend temporarily the preferential customs duty established under the stabilising mechanism.
Implementing measures
apply to every product which is put into free circulation after the date of entry into force of those measures.
apply provisional safeguard measures when there is a risk of serious damage to EU industry and there is evidence that the import of the product would cause damage which would be difficult to repair.
Provisional safeguard measures
The European Commission may adopt a provisional safeguard measure if:
there is sufficient evidence of a serious threat to the protection of EU industry caused by increased imports;
the imports are concentrated in an area where serious damage would be likely to be caused;
there are significant changes in the level of sales, production, productivity, capacity utilisation, profits and losses, and employment of the sector concerned.
If the Commission considers that the conditions for imposing the safeguard measure are met, it may initiate a proceeding. The request to initiate proceedings must contain evidence that:
the import of a particular product is likely to cause serious damage,
the level of imports are likely to result in serious damage and that the industry is adjusting to the situation;
serious damage could be caused by:
changes in the share of the domestic market taken by the increased imports,
increased imports and changes in production and productivity,
change in the levels of sales and production productivity, productivity and losses of the sectors concerned, and
the number of workers employed.
A decision terminating the investigation and proceedings without measures
is adopted by the Commission on the basis of the examination procedure referred to in Article 116 of the agreement.
Stabilisation mechanism
A mechanism for stabilising imports of bananas is set up under the Agreement. It suspends temporarily any preferential customs duties that have been reduced or eliminated as a consequence of reductions or elimination under the tariff elimination schedule for bananas. The stabilisation measures are:
suspended temporarily if imports of the same product have increased due to a reduction in the customs duty or reduction in a customs rate;
temporarily suspended if imports have increased because of a change in the rate of production, production or productivity, or because of changes in employment.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
   
It has applied since 11 December 2012 and had to become law in the Member States by 11 December 2016.
BACKGROUND
 
The EU–Central America Agreement on bananas was signed on 29 June 2012.
For more information, see:
Banana Agreement (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision (EU, Euratom) No 1888/2012 of 11 December 2011 on the conclusion of the Agreement on the Implementation of the Bilateral safeguard clause and the Stabilisation Mechanism for Bananas (Codified version) (OJ L 157, 11.12.2012, pp. 1-8)
RELATED DOCUMENTS
  Ебракован гандарска бантарка, годанка  городна   блактана вартала канханна,  кодланскогда гунарналкабак, кондласккална



Summary 96:
Preservation of funds held with credit institutions in the European Union (EU) — rules on judicial cooperation in civil matters relating to civil matters having cross-border implications [Official Journal C 191 of 29.6.2012].
Preservation OF Funds held with Credit Institutions
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2012 on the application of the principle of in personam to certain civil matters concerning the preservation of funds
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a legal instrument allowing a debtor to prevent a creditor who has not yet obtained a judgment, court settlement or authentic instrument from using the funds they have held with a credit institution.
The regulation applies to claims against a or the use of a credit card.
KEY POINTS
Conditions for issuing a Preservation Order
The debtor must be able to prove that he or she has not been the subject of a judgment or court settlement. The creditor must prove that they have not been subject to an authentic instrument. The debtor must also prove that:
the debtor has not committed a crime;
the creditor has not made a breach of his/her contractual obligations;
there has been no prior hearing of the debtor.
Where the creditor does not prove that the debtor’s claim is justified, it should not issue the order.
In the absence of a prior hearing, the debtor may apply for a preservation order in writing to a court or competent authority. The order must be in the official language of the institutions of the EU.
the order must contain all the information contained in the document transmitted by the debtor to the court or the creditor, including:
a description of the nature of the claim and the amount of the funds;
a list of the assets and liabilities of the creditor;
an explanation of the reasons for the preservation order; and
the name and address of the bank or entity responsible for preserving the funds.
Implementation of the order
The order is transmitted to the creditor or the court in the EU country in which the debtor is domiciled. The transmission must be done by the issuing court or creditor, depending on who is responsible under the law of the country of origin for initiating the enforcement procedure.
If the debtor does not comply with the conditions for issuing the order, the creditor may ask the court to issue an order in another EU country. The court or entity may refuse to do so if it considers that the order is inadmissible or unfounded.
Any documents to be addressed under this regulation may also be addressed in any other official language other than that of the European Parliament or the Council of the Union, if the Member State concerned has indicated that it can accept such other language.
A court or other competent authority may also refuse to issue such an order if the debtor fails to comply with certain conditions, such as:
notifying the other party of the existence of the document;
informing the court of any applications for an order that have been rejected;
notification of any information that has been rejected.
When an order is refused, the court must inform the debtor of the reason for the refusal, including the amount and duration of the refusal and the reasons why.
An order may be refused if:
there is no reason to believe that the creditor has committed a fraud or breach of its contractual obligations, or
there are grounds for doubt as to whether the debtor has been a party to a fraud, breach of a contract, breach or violation of a contractual obligation; or
the court has not held a hearing before the creditor.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Preservation order: an order which prevents a creditor from using funds that have not yet been paid.
* Creditor: any person or entity whose name or address is listed on a bank or other official document.
REFERENCES
Act
Entry into force - Date of expiry
Deadline for transposition in the Member States
Official Journal
