Summary 126:
EU trade mark system
Union trade mark systems
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 608/2013 on the European Union Trade Marks Office
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the registration and use of EU trade marks.
It codifies and repeals Regulations (EC) No 652/2013 and (EC), which had to become law in the EU countries by 23 March 2016.
KEY POINTS
   
The regulation sets out rules and procedural requirements for the EU trade mark office (EU Trade Mark Office).
It applies to collective and collective trade marks* as well as to trade mark certificates*.
It also applies to the use of trade marks obtained by registration.
EU trade marks
EU collective marks
Collective marks may be obtained by:
an application for a trade mark;
a certificate for a collective mark; or
a licence.
Use of a collective or collective trade mark
the use of a mark for the purpose of marketing goods or services.
A collective mark may be exclusive or non-exclusive.
Registration
The trade mark is registered in the register of the EU Trade Marks office and may be used for marketing goods and services in any EU Member State. It may also be used to mark products and services that are imported from outside the EU.
The register is maintained by the Office for the purposes of:
collecting, collating and validating collective marks;
registering collective marks and certificates for use;
checking the validity of collective marks for use in the goods they represent;
ensuring that collective marks are valid for a period of 5 years;
assisting in the exchange of information between EU countries.
assessing the validity and validity of EU collective marks or certificates.
Withdrawal, restriction, amendment and division of applications
If an application does not satisfy the requirements referred to in the regulation, the Office must withdraw, restrict, amend or withdraw the application. The applicant must notify the Office of the reasons for the withdrawal, restriction or division of application within 2 months of receiving the notification. The decision must be published in the Official Journal of the Office.
If the applicant fails to comply with the conditions laid down in this regulation, it must inform the Office and notify the proprietor of the goods it intends to place on the market.
In the event of infringements, the declarant or the holder of goods that the trade mark has been infringed, the owner of the mark is not entitled to prohibit the goods from being placed on the EU market in the country of final destination.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 23 March 2013.
BACKGROUND
Trade mark systems in Europe (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Collective trade mark: a mark that is used to describe a product or service which is used for the marketing of a product, service or service in a Member State and which has a legal personality.
* Certification: an official document issued by the European Commission to mark a product for sale in the Member State in which it is registered.

Summary 127:
Access to published works for persons who are blind, visually impaired or otherwise print-disabled (Marrakesh Treaty on Access to Published Works for Persons who are Blind, Visually Impaired, or otherwise Print Disabled)
Access to printed materials for persons with disabilities
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) 2017/1564 — facilitating access to accessible format copies of certain works and other protected subject matter
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to facilitate the making and dissemination of copies, in accessible formats, of certain copyright and related rights, and for the cross-border exchange of those copies.
The regulation applies to the following:
published works for the benefit of beneficiary persons;
public institutions or non-profit organisations that provide the same services to beneficiary persons as one of its primary activities, institutional obligations or as part of its public-interest missions.
Authorised entities established in an EU country may distribute, communicate or make available these accessible formats for non-commercial purposes.
Accessible formats include, for example, Braille, large print, adapted e-books, audio books and radio broadcasts.
Exports of accessible formats to non-EU countries
An authorised entity established in a Member State may export, communicate and make available accessible formats made in accordance with the implementation of the Marrakesh treaty, from a third country, by beneficiary persons in the EU and authorised entities established within the EU.
These accessible formats must comply with the following conditions:
they must be made in a language easily understood by persons with visual impairments or disabilities;
they cannot be read in a manner that would normally be normally acceptable for reading, insofar as, as a result of such impairments and disabilities, those persons are unable to read printed works to substantially the same degree as persons without such disabilities.
They must not be reproduced in a way that would be normally unacceptable for reading.
In addition, they must be protected against any infringement of copyright or related rights.
EU countries must ensure that these conditions are applied consistently throughout the internal market and do not jeopardise the harmonisation of exclusive rights and exceptions contained within those Directives.
Disputes between authorised entities and beneficiary persons are settled by means of a dispute settlement procedure.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 11 October 2017 and had to become law in the Member States by 11 October 2023.
BACKGROUND
This regulation is part of the EU’s efforts to promote the objectives of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) to facilitate access to printed works for people with disabilities. The FTEU aims to ensure that intellectual property rights do not constitute an unreasonable or discriminatory barrier to access to cultural materials.
For more information, see:
‘Access to accessible formats’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Accessible format: a format in which a person can read, write or listen to a printed work without having to move the eyes to the extent that would ordinarily be normally considered acceptable.

Summary 128:
Mutual assistance mechanism for widespread infringements with a European Union dimension (MUTUAL ASSISTANCE MECHANISM)
Mutual Assistance Mechanism
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2014 on mutual assistance for widespread infringement or widespread infringement with a Union dimension
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets up a mutual assistance mechanism between EU countries’ competent authorities and the European Commission to assist each other in the investigation and enforcement of infringements.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
any infringement of the EU’s consumer protection rules in relation to payment accounts services and credit agreements relating to residential immovable property;
any infringements of the European Banking Authority (EBA) rules in respect of payment accounts, credit agreements and other financial services;
the European Commission rules on the collection, classification and exchange of data on consumers’ accounts.
Competent authorities and their powers
EU countries must cooperate with each other and the Commission in the following areas:
the training of their officials involved in the application of this regulation;
collecting, classifying and exchanging data on consumer accounts;
coordinating investigations and enforcement measures.
The Commission must coordinate the functioning of the exchange of information.
Requests for information
Applicant authorities must submit a request for information to the competent authorities of other EU countries within 30 days of receiving a request from the Commission. The Commission must inform the applicant authorities of any information it receives from a trader.
A trader must comply with all requests for information, regardless of their form or format, their storage medium, or the place where they are stored.
If a trader fails to comply with the request, the requested authority must take appropriate enforcement measures, including:
implementing the commitments made by the trader;
imposing sanctions on the trader for similar infringements covered by this regulation.
Coordinated investigations
The competent authorities concerned must cooperate in coordinated investigations and enforcements.
When a trader commits an infringement, the competent authority concerned must:
ensure that the trader is held responsible for the infringement;
take all necessary measures to ensure that the infringement has ceased or has been prohibited in all EU countries concerned;
prohibit the trader from making any further infringements in the EU.
EU Member States may decide not to confer all the powers on every competent authority, provided that each of those powers can be exercised effectively and as necessary.
In addition, Member States must inform each other of their activities in the areas covered by the regulation in accordance with Article 10.
Commission Implementing Regulation (EC) No 2006/2004 provides for a review of the effectiveness of that regulation and its operational mechanisms.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
 
    Еганка бакова года  
It has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
  Маккодка  гонта 
The European Commission has adopted a number of implementing acts to modernise and modernise the mutual assistance system in the field of consumer protection. These include:
Directive 2014/17/EU on the protection of the collective economic interests of consumers in matters concerning payment accounts (Payment Account Services Directive) (see summary);
Directives 2014/92/EU and 2014/98/EU establishing the European Bank for Reconstruction and Development (European Banking Authority).
The EBA has also adopted a new penalty regime for infringements that fall within the scope of this Regulation.
For more information, see:
‘Mutual Assistance Mechanism’ on the Commission's website.

Summary 129:
In vitro diagnostic medical devices — safety and health — Regulation (EC) No 1907/2006 (see summary)
In vitro diagnostics medical devices – Regulation (EU) No 1906/2006
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU, Euratom) 2017/852 — in vitro diagnostic devices
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It sets out rules for the placing on the market and putting into service of in vitro medical devices (i.e. medical devices designed to diagnose, monitor and treat human health) in the European Union (EU).
It aims to ensure that these devices comply with the European Medicines Agency’s (EMA) Directive 2003/361/EC on medical devices.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
medical devices intended for use in the diagnosis, monitoring and treatment of human health and which are identified as having a risk to human health or to the environment;
devices intended for the diagnosis and monitoring of the health and well-being of persons who are incapacitated by an illness or injury;
diagnostic medical devices intended to be used in the treatment of diseases or injuries of the human body.
Manufacturers’ obligations
The manufacturer is responsible for:
designating the unit of device production;
assessing the technical documentation;
conducting conformity assessments of class D devices;
ensuring the safety and environmental performance studies;
checking that the devices meet the requirements laid down in the regulation are carried out according to scientific and ethical criteria;
monitoring and monitoring the devices’ performance;
implementing a post-market surveillance system.
Implementing Regulation (Evaluation of the regulation
The European Commission must submit a report to the European Parliament, the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions every 3 years on the implementation of the regulations. The report must include a justification, validation and verification of the solutions adopted to meet those requirements.
EU countries may apply this regulation also to: the manufacture of medical devices, their placing on sale and putting in service;
the placing into service, placing on sales and putting on service of devices; and
the monitoring of their compliance with the regulation.
The Commission must ensure that:
manufacturers and their authorised importers comply with all the requirements of this regulation;
regulatory authorities carry out inspections of the manufacturers’ compliance with this regulation and the requirements set out in Annex III;
EU Member States may apply the regulation to the manufacture, importer and distributor of devices, as well as to their place of business.
Member States may also apply this provision also to the manufacturer of devices and the importer or importer of devices placed on sale.
Authorisation of the manufacturer and importer
The EU Member States must:
authorise the manufacturer to authorise and authorise importers and importers to place on sale devices and to place into service devices placed into service by the manufacturer;
allow importers, importers or distributors to put into service medical devices which are not covered by the regulation and which do not comply with its requirements;
provide the manufacturer with a certificate of conformity and a technical documentation of the devices and their conformity assessment;
establish a monitoring system for the monitoring of compliance with these requirements. The monitoring system must be in place for at least 3 years and may be extended for a further 3 years.
Monitoring of compliance
The monitoring system should include:
a monitoring system of the device manufacturer and its authorised importer;
an electronic monitoring system;
a system for monitoring the safety, environmental and health performance of the products;
reporting to the competent authority of the Member States of any adverse incidents related to the devices. It must be able to identify and report such incidents to the relevant authorities.
Postmarket surveillance, vigilance and market surveillance
The Regulation sets out the responsibilities of:
the manufacturer of the medical devices and of the importers;
any other economic operator whose place of establishment is located in the Member State in which a medical device is placed on the EU market;
authorisations and authorisations granted by Member States for the manufacture and placing into the market of such devices. The regulation also sets out requirements on the monitoring and reporting of adverse incidents relating to these devices, including the notification of such incidents and the reporting of any such incidents.
In addition, Member States are required to establish a system for reporting adverse incidents and adverse events related to medical devices to the Commission and the European Agency for Safety and Health at Work (Safeguard).
The system must also be able:
to report adverse incidents to Safeguarding bodies;
to notify the European Commission of all adverse incidents that occur in the course of the monitoring or reporting of such adverse incidents;
notify the competent authorities of any incident that occurs in the context of the surveillance or reporting system. The Commission must also:
report to the SOH



Summary 130:
Ecodesign requirements for energy-related products
Ecodesensibilities for energy - appliances and fittings
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 on ecodesign requirements
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules on the sale, putting into service and putting on the market of energy-efficient appliances and electrical fittings.
It repeals Directive 2009/142/EC.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
all electrical appliances or fittings, whether new or second-hand, imported from a non-EU country;
new or secondhand electrical appliances* imported into the EU from a third country.
Manufacturers, importers and distributors are responsible for ensuring that the appliances or fitting comply with the requirements laid down in the regulation.
The manufacturer is responsible for drawing up the EU declaration of conformity, the manufacturer must assume responsibility for the compliance of the appliance or the fitting with the requirement laid down by the regulation and for the documentation attached to it.
Importers and distributors must ensure that:
the appliance or fitting bears the CE conformity marking;
the manufacturer affixes the CE marking on the appliance, the fitting or the appliance itself with the type and the year in which it was affixed to the appliance;
there is a conformity assessment carried out by a body designated by the EU countries’ competent national authorities;
in the event of a change in the type of type of appliance or of the manufacturer’s conformity assessment results, the national authorities must notify the competent authorities of the change in type of the conformity assessment.
Notified bodies must provide the other bodies carrying out similar conformity assessment activities with relevant information on issues relating to negative and, on request, positive conformity assessments results.
In addition, the European Commission and the European Atomic Energy Community (EEC) must ensure the transparency and the ability of the public to access the results of conformity assessment bodies’ work, in particular in relation to the safety requirements of Directive 2014/53/EU of the European Parliament and of the Council on the energy efficiency of electrical and electronic products.
EU declarations of conformity
The European Commission, the EEC and the Commission must:
ensure that the manufacturer of an appliance or a fitting bears responsibility for its compliance with the regulation;
assess the appliance and the fitting in the light of scientific and technical progress;
draw up an EU declaration declaring that the appliance meets the requirements set out in this regulation and that the fitting complies with them;
provide the competent authority of the EU country of notification with the information and documentation relating to the type, type and year of affixing of the CE markings;
make available to the public the information relating to type and type of fittings and the type or type of conformity of the appliances and the fittings;
publish the declaration and the certificate of conformity in accordance with Annex II of the regulation, in the form of a paper or electronic form.
Eco-design requirements
In order to meet the requirements, appliances must be so designed and constructed as to obviate any gas Abnormal fluctuation or failure of auxiliary energy or its restoration must not lead to an unsafe situation.
Annex III sets out the requirements for the design and construction of appliances, including:
design and construction;
design, construction and installation of appliances;
appliances, including the fitting and appliance itself, which must be designed, constructed and installed in such a way as to avoid any gas fluctuations or failures that could lead to a danger to human health or safety;
manufacturers’ responsibilities of distributors and importers;
importers’ obligations of distributors;
authorisations of importers to place appliances on the EU market;
information and documentation on the conformity of appliances and fitting.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
   
 
Directive 2014/35/EU on energy efficiency (see summary) sets out a framework for the setting of ecodeign requirements. It repeals and repeals Council Directives 89/686/EEC and 93/15/EC on technical harmonisation and standards and Directives 94/9/EC, 94/25/EC and 95/16/EC concerning the safety of electrical appliances.
For more information, see:
Energy efficiency (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Ecodesign: the aim of which is to reduce the environmental impact of energy consumption.
* Conformity assessment: the assessment of whether a product meets the essential requirements of the legislation.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  Егандарска бакова гактанка: a technical assessment of an electrical or electronic product to determine whether it complies



Summary 131:
Cross-border transport of euro cash by road: cash-in-transit (CIT)
Cross-Border transport of euros by road
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1072/2009 — cross-border CIT licence
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European Union (EU) system for the cross-Border Transport of Euro Cash by Road.
It sets out the conditions for the issuing and holding of a licence for the transport by road of euro-denominated cash in CIT vehicles.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
cash-in–transit companies operating in the euro area, banks, the large retail sector and other professional cash handlers that offer the best price and/or service and to take advantage of the cash services of the nearest national central bank (NCB) branch or CIT cash centre, even if it is located in another EU country.
Companies holding a licence may transport euro coins by road using an unarmoured CIT vehicle carrying only coins, provided that the following conditions are met:
the vehicle is of ordinary appearance;
there are at least two CIT security staff per vehicle;
none of the security staff wears a uniform;
the CIT company’s owner is established in the EU country in whose territory the vehicle is established.
Applicants for a licence must submit the following documents:
a valid for a maximum period of 4 weeks;
an original or certified copy of a valid for up to 4 years;
a copy of the licence;
ad hoc training module as detailed in the annex to the regulation;
proof that the applicant has been authorised by the issuing authority.
The applicant must provide the competent authority in the country of origin, the host EU country or the Member State of transit with the following information:
place of departure, maximum duration and number of euro deliveries/pick-ups per day;
number of CIT deliveries/picks-up;
type of vehicle used;
location of the CIT centre;
name of the company;
date and time of the ad hoc initial training.
In addition, the applicant must:
provide the competent authorities of the EU countries of origin and of the Member States of transit of the euro cash;
submit a copy of an original or a certified copy to the authority in charge of issuing the licence.
If necessary, the Commission may issue an emergency security measure to protect the safety and security of the passengers and crew of the vehicle. This measure must be effective, proportionate and dissuasive. It may be temporary or permanent depending on the nature or severity of the infringement.
Transport of euro coins
Companies may also transport euro cash using an IBNS model used by CIT companies using IBNS vehicles. However, due to the specific characteristics of the IBNS vehicle, it is normal practice for a CIT van to carry out a much larger number of deliveries or picks-up per day.
FROM WHEN DOES THIS REGULATIONS APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Cross-Border CIT: a company that transports euro cash between participating EU countries by road.
* Euro cash: euro cash delivered or picked-up by road in a vehicle carrying coins.

Nutrition labelling of foods — rules for the labelling and labelling in the European Union (EU) — rules on the indication of origin and the content of the nutrition declaration (Article 9 of Regulation (EU)*
Nutrition Labelling of food — rules governing the indication, labelling, packaging and presentation of foods in the EU
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 1169/2011 on nutrition labelling
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down rules for labelling foods and food information law.
It aims to ensure that foods on the EU’s internal market are safe and wholesome.
KEY POINTS

Foods must be labelled with the following information:
the energy value;

The energy value must be expressed on the basis of per portion or per consumption unit alone. It must include the energy value together with the amounts of fat, saturates, sugars, and salt, as well as the amount of protein, protein, carbohydrate, fat, protein and carbohydrate.
In cases where foods require special storage conditions or/or conditions of use, those conditions must be indicated.
Additional mandatory particulars for specific types or categories of foods are listed in Annex II.
Annex III sets out the substances or products causing allergies or intolerances and the name of the substance or product must be accompanied by a reference.
the indication of the substances and products causing allergies or injurious to health.
If a food is not recommended for children or pregnant women, it must contain the word ‘contains’ in the same field of vision as the name, followed by an indication of any other written or pictorial matter or any other intervening material.

food information law

Summary 133:
Issuing of euro coins
Issuance of Euro coins
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 974/98 on the introduction of the euro
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the issuing and circulation of 2-euro coins and 2-centre commemorative coins to celebrate specific subjects.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all EU countries whose currency is the euro. It does not apply to:
non-euro countries that do not have a single currency;
euro countries which do not issue euro coins.
Issues of circulation coins
EU countries may issue two types of euro coin: circulation coins and collector coins. These coins are intended to commemorate a specific subject and comply with the denominations and technical specifications laid down in the regulation.
Collector coins are euro coins intended for collection that are not issued with a view to their entry into circulation. The regulation sets limits on the number of collector coins that can be issued per year and per issuing EU country.
The total number of coins put into circulation for each individual issue must not exceed the higher of the following two ceilings:
0,1 % of the cumulated total net number of 2 euro coins put in circulation by all euro countries up to the beginning of the year preceding the regulation’s entry into force; and
0.1% of the total net numbers of 2 cent coins put on the market.
Commemorative coins
The Commission must establish certain volume limits for commemorative euro coins in order to ensure that such coins remain a minor percentage of the overall number of the 2-Euro coins in circulation.
In addition, the Commission must conduct an impact assessment on the continued issuance of 1-euro and 1-and-2-cent coins. This assessment must include a cost-benefit analysis which takes into account the real production costs of those coins set against their value and benefits. The Commission may decide whether to issue a common design collectively issued by all the euro countries. The decision whether to do so is taken by the Council of the European Union (EU).
In accordance with the regulation, coins denominated in euro and cent and complying with the denomination, technical specifications and the design laid down by the Commission have the status of legal tender in all EU Member States.
References

Summary 134:
The European Social Fund (ESF) — mission and scope
The European social fund (ESSF)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1303/2013 on the mission and the scope of the European social Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the EU’s mission and its scope, along with the specific investment priorities addressing the thematic objectives, and lays down specific provisions concerning the type of activities that may be financed by the ESF.
It repeals and repeals Regulation (EC) No 1081/2006.
KEY POINTS
The ESF is the European Union's (EU's) social innovation and transnational cooperation (SINCE) fund. Its main objective is to promote social inclusion and combating poverty, in particular with regard to disadvantaged people such as the Roma. It also aims to contribute to the creation of jobs, the mobility of workers, the social inclusion of workers and the social entrepreneurship of young people.
Its objectives are to:
promote social inclusion by:
encouraging young people to participate in the labour market;
promoting job creation;
increasing employability;
supporting the social dialogue and strengthening of social dialogue;
contributing to social entrepreneurship.
In order to achieve these objectives, the European Commission has adopted the Integrated Guidelines on the European System of Social Innovation and Transnational Cooperation (SSIC), which set out the priority axes for the implementation of ESF projects.
the ESF supports the social innovation, social entrepreneurship and social innovation.
The SINVENTION
The EU countries must ensure that:
the social partners are involved in ESFormalising young people in the social economy;
young people are actively engaged in job-searching and job-seeking activities;
participants in education/training are actively involved in job searching;
EU countries and the regions are encouraged to leverage ESF through financial instruments in order to support, for example, students, job creation, job mobility and social inclusion.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLYouth Employment Initiative (YEI) apply?
From 1 January 2014.
Participation in the YEI is open to young people from all EU countries, regardless of their age, gender or nationality. The aim is to improve the quality of life for young people and their families and to reduce the social exclusion of disadvantaged people, especially Roma.
YEI participants are:
students;
employees;
workers’ organisations;
social partners;
professional associations;
organisations.
Eligible beneficiaries
The ESI covers young people who are unemployed, underemployed or unemployed and who have no job prospects. The ESI also covers people who do not have a job but who are actively seeking a job or who have the potential to find one.
BACKGROUND
The Social Innovation Fund (SIC) is the EU's social innovation fund. It is funded by cohesion policy funding.
For more information, see:
European Social Fund and the SIC (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Youth Employment Initiative: an initiative to encourage young people, particularly Roma, to take part in the employment market.

Summary 135:
European demographic statistics — EU countries’ data (2013-2027) (European statistical system committee)
European statistical systems committee
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 182/2011 — European demographic statistics
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a common legal framework for the production and dissemination of European statistics at European level.
It sets out the principles and procedures for the European statistical system (ESS).
KEY POINTS
EU countries must provide the European Commission (Eurostat) with data on the total population at national level for specific EU purposes every year.
The data must be based on:
live births by sex, month of occurrence, live birth-order, mother’s age, mother's year of birth, mother-country-of-birth, country of citizenship and mother's region of residence;
deaths by age, sex, year-of birth, region of origin and country of residence.
Data sources
Eurostat must use the data sources chosen by the EU countries, in accordance with national law and practice.
National and European statistical authorities, and, where applicable, other relevant national and regional authorities, should take account of the principles set out in the European Statistics Code of Practice, as reviewed and updated by the European Statistical System Committee on 28 September 2011.
EU statistics transmitted to the Commission
The Commission must ensure the quality of the data transmitted to Eurostat, including:
data sources are based on the national statistical institutes and national authorities’ own data sources;
the data sources selected by Eurostat are:
based on the data they receive from Eurostat;
selected on the basis of the results of the feasibility studies referred to in Article 5 of Regulation (EC) No 223/2009 on the European statistics code of practice;
transmitted to the Eurostat by national and European statistics authorities, Eurostat and Eurostat on their own initiative;
consistent with the principles of professional independence, impartiality, objectivity, reliability, statistical confidentiality and cost effectiveness.
In order to facilitate the carrying out these studies, the Commission may provide financial support to the national statistics institutes or other national authorities.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
The regulation applies from 1 January 2013.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission is responsible for producing and disseminating European statistics. It is assisted in this task by the ESS Committee.

European statistics (European Commission).

Summary 137:
European Maritime and Fisheries Fund (EMFF) - general principles
European Maritime & Fisheries Fund(EMFF)*
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1380/2013 establishing the European Maritime and fisheries Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes the EMFF to support the implementation of the Convention on the Functioning of the European Union’s (CFP) fisheries policy.
It repeals Regulation (EC) No 761/2001.
KEY POINTS
The EMFF is a European maritime and fisheries fund established under the CFP. It aims to:
promote sustainable and selective fishing in EU waters;
contribute to the sustainable management and management of marine ecosystems;
support the development and implementation of conservation measures and regionalisation;
encourage participation and cooperation between EU countries in designing and implementing conservation measures, regionalisation and coastal and rural regions.
The objectives of the fund include:
fostering the implementation and sustainable management of the IMP;
promoting human capital, job creation and social dialogue;
providing environmental services.
Support for business start-up
EMFF supports:
the design, development and monitoring of technical and administrative means necessary to develop and implement conservation measures;
the promotion of human capital and job creation;
environmental services;
participation of stakeholders in conservation measures.
In addition, EMFF provides technical assistance to the national programmes and the management and use of data for scientific analysis and CFP implementation.
Funding
The total financial contribution from the EU to the measures referred to in Article 29(4) of the regulation is not more than 5 % of the EU financial support allocated per EU country.
EU countries must designate the managing authorities responsible for the project. The EMFF may grant financial support to projects that fulfil the following criteria:
contributing to sustainable fishing;
fishing capacity reduction;
preventing the spread of invasive species;
protecting marine ecosystems.
Aquaculture provides environmental services, including aquaculture providing environmental services and aquacultural training.
Fisheries policy
The European Union fisheries policy is based on a number of principles:
conservation of the marine environment;
sustainable management of fisheries;
protection of marine biodiversity;
management of marine resources;
monitoring of marine environment and marine ecosystems, including the use of scientific and technical data;
scientific and technical assistance for the development of marine and coastal research;
assistance for the implementation, monitoring and management, of the conservation and management measures and the regionalisation of fisheries policies.
National programmes
The EU countries must submit a national programme for the period from 1 January 2014 to 31 December 2020 to the European Commission. The programme must include the methods for selecting and implementing the operational programme, the description of the strategy, the targets and measures to be taken for the reduction of the fishing capacity in accordance with Article 22 of Regulation (EU), and a description of how the measures are to be implemented. The operational programme must also include the method for selecting the managing authority responsible for implementing the strategic plan.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
    дарга баркова  
It has applied since 31 December 2013.
BACKGROUND
 
The CFP was reformed in 2013. The new CFP aims to improve the management of EU fisheries and to promote sustainable fishing.
For more information, see:
‘Fishing’ (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Fishing capacity: the total number of fish caught in an individual year.
* Aquaculture: the production and management by a company or organisation of aquatic resources, such as fish, crustaceans, mussels, oysters and clams.
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 138:
Insurance-based investment products — key investor information
Insurance–related investment products – key information
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1094/2010 on the key information document for insurance-backed investment products for retail investors
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out minimum requirements for the marketing, presentation and disclosure of key information documents for insurance products to retail investors.
KEY INFORMATION DOCUMENT
The regulation sets out a standardised format which allows retail investors to compare different PRIIPs, since consumer behaviour and capabilities are such that they must be carefully calibrated to maximise understanding and use of information.
It also sets out rules on the disclosure of product information requirements, including:
the format, presentation, content and content of information;
the type and nature of the infringement; and
the identity of the persons responsible.
Key information document
A PRIIP may satisfy the requirements of the regulation by providing the following information to a person with written authority to make investment decisions on behalf of the retail investor:
a description of the product’s investment features;
a summary of the risks and risks associated with the product;
an explanation of how the product works.
The document must be accurate, fair, clear and not misleading.
An explanatory statement must appear directly underneath the title of the document.
A person advising on, or selling an insurance-related investment product may also provide the following additional information:
an estimate of the risk and the product may entail;
how the product is likely to perform in the future.
the amount of money a retail investor will be able to take out of the investment portfolio
the expected to be put back into the investment.
In addition, the document must contain:
investment objectives
a list of investment strategies
a breakdown of the assets and liabilities of the company
a statement on the risk profile of each investment strategy
a risk profile for each investment solution
the number of assets that can be taken out of an investment portfolio.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLACE INTO FORCE?
 
   
It has applied since 1 January 2011. EU countries had to incorporate it into national law by 1 January 2012.
BACKGROUND
  (European Commission)
KEY TERMS
* Insurance-based insurance investment product: a product that provides investment solutions tailored to the needs of retail investors, is frequently combined with insurance coverage or can be complex and difficult to understand.
* Key information document: a document containing information on a product, such as:
its investment features and risks,
the risks and benefits associated with it,
its risks, and
its expected future performance.

Summary 139:
Single Resolution Fund (SRM) — rules for the management of insolvent entities
Single Resolution Funds (SRMs) — ways for insolvency to be resolved
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 575/2013 establishing the Single Resolution Fund
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules and procedures for the resolution of failing or likely to fail entities in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation establishes the European Resolution Fund, a body responsible for managing the assets and liabilities of entities that are insolvent.
The European Commission is responsible for appointing the Board of the SRM, which is chaired by the European Central Bank (ECB) and composed of representatives of the national competent authorities of the participating EU countries.
It is composed of the ECB, the ECB and the national resolution authorities. It meets at least once a year.
Its tasks include:
drawing up resolution plans for institutions and groups;
assisting the national authorities in the preparation of the resolution plans;
ensuring that national authorities are informed of the financial situation of the entities concerned.
In addition, the Board must:
ensure that the assets of the entity are, or are likely in the near future to be, less than its liabilities;
take appropriate measures to ensure that the entity is not unable to pay its debts as they fall due;
provide the competent national authorities with the information they need to make a decision on the resolution plan;
make available to the public the information it needs in order to assess the state of an entity’s financial situation;
implement procedures to ensure the proper functioning of the institution and group.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
The Single Resolution Facility (SRF) was set up in 2013. It was designed to help the European banking sector cope with the impact of the 2008 financial crisis.
For more information, see:
Single resolution fund (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT

Summary 140:
Noise operating restrictions at EU airports
Noise operations
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 691/2010 on noise operating restrictions
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules on the introduction of noise-related operating restrictions* at European Union airports.
It aims to facilitate the achievement of specific noise abatement objectives, including health aspects, at the level of individual airports, while respecting relevant EU rules, in particular those laid down in Directive 2002/49/EC, and the legislation within each EU country.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all airports in the European Union (EU). It does not apply to aircraft such as military aircraft and aircraft undertaking customs, police and fire-fighting operations.
The objective of the regulation is to enable the use of operating restrictions in accordance with the so-called ‘balanced approach’, which aims to ensure the sustainable development of the airport and air traffic management network capacity from a gate-to-gate perspective.
Rules on noise mitigation measures
EU countries must ensure that:
noise performance information is obtained in a transparent manner and that it is accessible to relevant authorities and stakeholders;
the cost-effectiveness of any new operating restriction is assessed, including, where relevant, their cross-border impact;
local residents, or their representatives, and relevant local authorities are consulted, and that technical information is provided to them;
measures are provided to mitigate the effects of the noise.
the number of aircraft operating at an airport and the number of people affected by the noise must be calculated.
A decision-making procedures must be in line with the objective of achieving the objectives.
Regulations (EU countries’ national legislation on noise-based noise management must be amended to take account of:
the impact of noise on human health and the environment;
airport capacity;
environmental aspects; and
air traffic management.
Repeal
The European Commission must report to the European Parliament and to the Council on the application of this regulation by 14 June 2021.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
From 14 June 2010.
BACKGROUND
   
The EU has adopted a number of rules in the field of noise management. These include:
Directive 2002/48/EC on common rules for the allocation of slots at European airports (see summary);
Commission Regulation (EC) No 2096/2005 laying down common requirements for the provision of air navigation services and network functions and amending Regulations (EC, EEC, Euratom) No 2111/2006 and (EC), EEC and Euratom.
For more information, see:
‘Noise management’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 141:
Cross-border insolvency proceedings: common rules for insolvencies and the coordination of proceedings between practitioners
Cross-Border insolvencs: common Rules for the administration of cross-border proceedings
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EU) No 1215/2012 on the application of certain of the provisions of Regulation (EC) No 1346/2000 relating to insolvent proceedings
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the rules for the effective administration of insolvencations in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to proceedings relating to:
the debtor’s assets and liabilities;
the assets of the debtor in possession;
contracts relating to immoveable property.
It does not apply to proceedings on creditors’ claims relating to the debtor's assets.
Right to request the opening of proceedings
Creditors who have their habitual residence, domicile or registered office in an EU country must be informed about the opening or opening of the proceedings related to their assets. They must also be informed of the conditions under which the proceedings are to be opened. The proceedings must be open to all creditors, irrespective of their nationality.
The proceedings must respect the fundamental rights and obligations of all persons, including the right to be heard and to be represented by an independent lawyer.
In addition, the regulation provides for the right of the creditor to participate in other proceedings on their behalf. These include:
participation in other than those relating to their own assets;
access to the assets of a debtor in the proceedings;
appointment of a lawyer;
right to be informed in writing of the opening and closing of proceedings.
right of access to a court in another EU country.
the right of a creditor to access the proceedings of another court in a non-EU country in which proceedings have been opened.
Cooperation and communication between courts
The European Court of Justice (ECJ) is responsible for coordinating the proceedings between courts in the EU countries. It is assisted by a coordinator. The coordinator must communicate with a court with the aim of:
coordinating the proceedings in the relevant EU countries;
ensuring the proper functioning of the judicial system;
promoting the proper application of the law of the EU country where proceedings are opened;
protecting the rights of creditors in the event of fraudulent or abusive forum shopping.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
It entered into force on 1 January 2014.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
Interinstitutional proceedings (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Creditors: all persons who are entitled to be treated as creditors in a court of law in a case of bankruptcy.
* Court: the court which delivers a judgment in the case of a bankruptcy case.

Summary 142:
Athens Convention relating to the carriage of passengers and their luggage by sea (OJ L 94, 30.3.1994, pp. 1-8)
Athens Agreement relating to passenger and their luggage by sea
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2004 on liability rules for damage caused to passengers in the event of maritime accidents
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that liability rules are in place for passengers involved in maritime accidents.
It is based on the 1974 Athens Convention on the Carriage of Passengers and their Luggage by Sea and the Protocol of 2002 to the Convention.
KEY POINTS
The Convention:
lays down the liability limits applicable to the carrier and the performing carrier for the loss of or damage to cabin luggage;
sets out the general limits of liability for death and personal injury;
requires insurance companies to cover the costs of damage caused by passengers.
Carriers and performing carriers:
are liable for:
the loss of, damage to, or delay in the arrival of the ship;
the delay resulting from labour disputes;
delays resulting from a labour dispute.
The liability of the carrier:
may exceed 2 250 units of account per passenger, per carriage;
may not exceed the highest amount which could be awarded against either the carrier or the performing carriers under this Convention;
is not liable for death or personal injury.
Insurance companies:
must:
ensure that passengers’ travel insurance covers the cost of loss or damage;
provide passengers with a notice of loss and damage to their luggage before departure;
make sure that passengers have a valid travel insurance policy;
notify the authorities in the issuing country if they believe that the conditions under which they have been issued are not complied with.
In addition, insurance companies must ensure that:
travel insurance covers:
damage caused to the cabin;
delay resulting from any labour dispute or labour dispute;
any delays resulting from the labour dispute, labour disputes or labour disputes.
Liability limits:
carrier and performing carrier are liable for loss of:
cabin;
luggage;
disputes arising from the carriage performed by a performing carrier;
defects arising from labour relations between the parties.
Claimants:
have the right to be compensated for loss caused to their baggage;
are entitled to a minimum of 10% of the total value of the goods lost or damaged.
Limits of liability:
each party is liable for the total amount of the damage caused, including:
loss or damage resulting from:
delay or delay resulting in labour disputes and labour disputes,
delay resulting from disputes between parties or labour relations,
delay, delay or delay arising from a dispute between parties and labour relations.
Defendants:
any person acting negligently, recklessly or with knowledge that such damage would result,
anyone acting with intent to cause such damage, or recklessly and with knowledge of such damage.
Implementing Regulation (EU) 2019/852 amends Regulation (EC), adding the following to the list of liability limits.
the liability limits are:
limit of liability applicable to:
death and bodily injury,
personal injury, and
loss of property;
damage to property, including loss of property and loss of its contents.
If the liability limit is exceeded, the claimant must:
make a formal request to the competent authority of the EU country in which the accident took place;
issue a certificate in the official language or language of the issuing EU country;
draw up a claim for compensation.
An EU country may, at its own discretion, withdraw these certificates if it considers that they have not been issued in accordance with the conditions set out in the regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGISLATION APPLY?
    банкала гарода
It has applied since 30 June 2004.
BACKGROUND
 
  абалка is one of the most important legal instruments in the field of maritime transport. It has been amended several times, most recently by the 2004 Protocol of the International Maritime Organisation (IMO).
For more information, see:
‘The Athens Convention’ on the European Commission’s website.
* KEY TERMS
* Carriage: the transport of passengers by sea.
Performing carrier: any person or organisation acting within the scope of their employment who is responsible for the carriage or delivery of a passenger.
Accident: any act which causes or is likely to cause death or bodily injury to a person or body.
Disputes between parties: any dispute between persons or bodies over the management of a ship or its cargo.

Summary 143:
Regulation (EU) No 552/2010 on the management of freight corridors
Regulation(EU) 2018/852 — management of rail freight
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out rules for managing freight corridors* on the European Union’s railway network.
It aims to ensure that rail freight traffic is managed, regulated and secured.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to all freight corridors within the EU. It does not apply to:
the existing freight corridors established by the Member States;
the new freight corridors created by the European Commission;
new freight corridors proposed by Member States.
Management
The management board of a freight corridor is the body responsible for managing the rail freight market on the freight corridor. It is composed of representatives of the infrastructure managers of the freight corridors concerned. It comprises:
infrastructure managers;
management board members;
executive board;
transport bodies;
international pre-arranged train paths for freight trains;
administrative bodies.
Infrastructure managers must:
ensure that the management board has the legal status, the establishment of its organisational structure, resources and staffing, on the basis of mutual consent of the railway infrastructure managers concerned;
make investment plans for the development and operation of the corridor;
take decisions regarding its legal status and the organisation of its management board.
In addition, the board must periodically review the implementation plan taking into account progress made in its implementation and performance measured in accordance with the objectives referred to in the objectives of the regulation and the objectives set out in the regulation.
Investment in the freight market
investment plans must be published to ensure applicants who may operate in the corridor are well informed.
Selection of further freight corridors and the modification of the existing ones
The selection of additional freight corridors must take account of the following criteria:
crossing by the corridor of the territory of at least three Member States, or of two Member States if the distance between the terminals served by the rail corridor is greater than 500 km;
conformity with the TEN (Transport for European Union Railways) directive;
availability of rail infrastructure;
capacity allocated to freight trains.
Priority rules may also mean priority targets depending on the situation in the respective Member State.
Transport bodies
The European Transport Agency (ETA) is responsible for coordinating the development of the European rail network and for the coordination of the various bodies responsible for the management and organisation of the rail network, including the management boards.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLY?
Directive 2010/204/EU has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
   
For more information, see:
Railways (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
* Freight corridor: a rail freight route between a rail terminal and a freight rail yard.
* International pre-arrival train path: an international rail route between two or more rail terminals.

Council Regulation (EU), Euratom, Euratom of 21 December 2010 on the Management of Railways (OJ L 204, 21.1.2010, pp. 1-8)

Summary 144:
Road transport operators: professional qualification
Road transport professionals: professional qualifications
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EEC) No 552/2010 on the professional qualification of road transport operators
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the requirements for the professional qualifications of road haulage and passenger transport operators in the European Union (EU).
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to all road transport undertakings operating in the EU. It does not apply to undertakings that have been established in non-EU countries.
Requirements for the qualification
To be qualified as a road transport operator, the applicant must:
have a degree in the field of transport;
be familiar with road transport and its aspects;
have been involved in road transport activities for at least 10 years;
participate in the activities of a transport undertaking or a road passenger transport undertaking in one or more EU countries for the period of 10 years before 4 December 2009.
The applicant must be familiar with the following:
the role and function of the various social institutions which are concerned with road transportation (trade unions, works councils, employers’ organisations, etc.);
the responsibilities and obligations of the undertaking and its management.
Examination
EU countries may decide to exempt from the examinations referred to in Article 8, persons who provide proof that they have continuously managed a road hauler or passenger undertaking for a period of more than 10 years.
Certificates of professional competence
The competent authority of an EU country must issue the following certificates:
a certificate of competence with at least 2 visible characters (e.g. ‘1’ and ‘2’) in the form of a hologram or light-emitting diodes;
certificates relating to financial standing;
a declaration made in accordance with Article 3.3.3 of the regulation.
In addition, the competent authority may require an undertaking whose authorisation has been suspended or withdrawn to ensure that its transport undertaking no longer fulfils the requirements laid down in this regulation. This may result in the loss of good repute.
Penalties
The European Commission must draw up a list of categories, types and degrees of seriousness of serious infringements of Community rules which, in addition to those set out in Annex IV, may lead to the loss or revocation of the authorisation of an undertaking. The penalties provided for shall be effective, proportionate and dissuasive.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
The Regulation has applied since 4 December 2010. It had to become law in the Member States by 4 December 2011.
BACKGROUND
Road Transport Operators: Professional Qualifications (European Commission).
For more information, see:
‘Road Transport’ on the European Commission’s website.

Summary 145:
Social security: rules on the application of social security schemes to employed persons and their families moving within the EU (Regulation (EC) No 883/2004 on the procedure for implementing Regulation (EU) No 1408/71 on social security systems to employees and their family members moving across the European Union
Social security rules: how social security institutions apply Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 574/72
SUMMARY OF:
Council Regulation (EEC), Euratom — Rules on the implementation of Regulations (EC and EFTA) No 908/2004 and (EU, Eurat) No 1052/2004 relating to social security
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATIONS?
   
 
The regulation sets out rules on how the social security system is implemented in the EU. It aims to improve the functioning of the system and to ensure that people covered by the regulation are able to access their rights as quickly as possible and under optimum conditions.
KEY POINTS
Scope
This regulation applies to:
social security schemes for employment, employment, self-employment or residence completed under the legislation of an EU Member State;
the social security scheme for which a person is employed or staying in another Member State.
It does not apply to certain types of insurance (e.g. life insurance, sickness insurance, long-term care insurance, medical insurance, etc.).
It applies to all periods of insurance completed in the Member State of stay, except for periods of life insurance which are considered as sickness insurance.
Beneficiaries (i.e.
periods of insurance for which are not covered by national legislation).
It also applies to periods of self-employed or residence which are covered as long as they do not overlap with periods of employment or residence.
In addition, it applies to family benefits which are provided by the institution of the last Member State whose legislation was applicable to the person concerned and who are covered by that Member State’s legislation.
Procedures
When a person applies for social security benefits, they must inform the institution responsible or the scheme applicable or for designating periods to a specific scheme, taking into account:
the place of residence or stay,
the duration of the period of insurance and
the nature of the sickness insurance benefits.
The institution responsible must:
make an initial determination on the validity of the claim;
make a final decision on whether the claim is valid or not;
recover the costs of the claims;
prohibit the institution from rejecting a claim.
If a claim is rejected, the institution must reimburse the costs within the limits of and under the conditions of the reimbursement rates laid down in its legislation, without the agreement of the insured person.
A dispute concerning a particular claim may not hinder the reimbursement of other claims or other claims.
Where a claim has been rejected, it must be reviewed in writing. The person concerned must be notified of the result of the review in writing and of the conditions under which the claim may be reimbursed.
When an institution rejects a claim, the person who made the claim must be informed of the reasons for the rejection and of any other procedures that may be applicable.
Recovery of claims
The person who makes a claim must have the right to recover the costs incurred. The amount of the recovery must be as close as possible to actual expenditure. The interest rate must be calculated on the basis of the reference rate applied by the European Central Bank to its main refinancing operations.
FROM WHEN DO THE LEGISLATION AND REGULATION APPLY?
The regulations have applied since 1 January 2005.
They apply from 1 January 2006.
BACKGROUND
The European Commission has adopted a number of measures to ensure the proper application of the regulation. These include:
improving cooperation between social security authorities and institutions;
establishing a liaison body in each Member State to receive and respond to claims and to exchange information;
introducing a system for the exchange of information between institutions and persons concerned and employers.
For more information, see:
‘Social security’ on the European Commission's website.
* KEY TERMS
* Social security scheme: a scheme that provides benefits to people who are employed or stay in an EU country for the duration of their employment or stay.

Summary 146:
Public health and health and safety at work: Eurostat’s statistical system
Public healthcare and safety: Eurostats’ statistical system (2008-2013)
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on the establishment of a European statistical system in the area of occupational safety and health at work
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes a European system for collecting and disseminating comparable data and information in the field of public health and at work.
KEY POINTS
The European Union (EU) has adopted a second programme of Community action for health (2008–2013) which aims to generate and disseminate health information and knowledge. This programme includes a sustainable health monitoring system with mechanisms for collection comparable data, with appropriate indicators, and to develop, with the European Statistical Programme (Eurostat), the statistical element of this system.
Eurostat collects data on:
public health and occupational safety;
accidents at work;
health and safety in the workplace;
personal health and well-being;
social aspects of health.
The Commission (EuroStat) collects the data on those areas through administrative sources. It also works in cooperation with the United Nations and its special organisations, such as the World Health Organisation (WHO) and the International Labour Organisation (ILO), as well as the Organisation for Economic Cooperation and Development (OECD), when relevant and possible.
In addition, Eurostat works closely with international organisations.
This regulation sets out the characteristics, namely variables, definitions and classifications of the subjects covered by this regulation.
It also defines the characteristics of the categories of occupational accidents at work, and the types of occupational diseases and occupational accidents, as defined by Eurostat.
These characteristics are defined according to the following criteria:
type of activity;
duration of exposure;
number of hours worked;
type and duration of exposure to risk factors;
degree of risk factor;
types of risk factors.
EU countries’ national statistical systems must take account of the different national systems and avoid imposing additional administrative burdens on the Commission. The Commission must also take the necessary steps to improve the dissemination, accessibility and documentation of the statistical information, in accordance with the principles of comparability, reliability and statistical confidentiality laid down in the European Data Protection Supervisor Regulation.

Summary 147:
Quality of job vacancy statistics: quarterly production
Quality of jobs vacancies: quarterly collection
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 582/2003 on the production of statistics on Community job vacancies
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It lays down the requirements for the regular quarterly production of European Union (EU) statistics on job vacancies.
It is part of the European Employment Strategy for monitoring and analysis of the level and structure of labour demand.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation covers all economic activities defined by the common classification system for economic activities in the EU (NACE) in force, except for the activities of households as employers and activities of extraterritorial organisations and bodies.
EU countries must produce the data using business surveys. They must also transmit back data for at least the four quarters preceding the quarter for which data are to be provided on the first data delivery.
Quality
The Commission (Eurostat) assesses the quality of the data transmitted by EU countries and Eurostat, the European Union’s statistical office, and the European Economic and Social Committee (EESC).
Eurostat may also establish and coordinate sample schemes to produce Community estimates where national sample schemes do not meet the EU requirements with regard to quarterly data collection.
National authorities must ensure that the data are shared with the social partners at national and European level and that the relevant information is made available to the European Commission.
References and technical specifications
The European Commission must:
analysearise the specifications for the data;
assess the quality and timeliness of data transmitted;
make available to Eurostat the metadata needed to interpret the changes in the data arising from either methodological or technical changes;
provide the European Parliament, the Council and the Commission with reports on the quality.
FROM WHEN DOES IT APPLYEAR OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
   
It entered into force on 1 January 2004.
BACKGROUND
The Regulation on Community Statistics (EEC) is one of a series of measures designed to improve the quality, reliability and comparability of EU statistics. The other measures are:
the Action Plan on EMU Statistical Requirements, which was endorsed by the Council on 29 September 2000, and subsequent progress reports on implementation of that plan, identified as a priority the development of a legal basis covering job vacancies statistics.

Summary 148:
Hybrid vehicles: type-approval requirements for hydrogen containers and systems
Hybrid cars and systems: type of approvals
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2008 on type-applications for hydrogen-powered vehicles
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It sets out the requirements for the European Union (EU) type approval of hydrogen containers designed to use compressed (gaseous) hydrogen and systems.
It also sets out rules for the testing and certification of these containers.
KEY POINTS
Requirements
The regulation applies to:
hydrogen containers* and systems* intended for use in hydrogen vehicles;
vehicle interface systems*;
excess flow systems;
overpressure protection systems; and
heat exchanger failure detection systems. It does not apply to hydrogen systems designed to be installed in the hydrogen system itself.
Requirements for containers
Container types must meet the following requirements:
the container must be pressurised to working pressure;
the containers must be free from leakage;
they must be able to withstand a temperature cycle of at least 3 degrees Celsius;
there must be no signs of visible permanent deformation or visible leaks.
There must be a minimum number of internal leakage and a maximum number of external leakage devices.
The test procedures must be carried out in accordance with the requirements set out in the regulation’s annexes.
National authorities must submit a report to the European Commission every 5 years on the performance of the hydrogen containers, including the number of cycles to failure and the number and location of the leaks. The report must include:
a description of the tests carried out;
a list of the components and systems that have been tested;
an estimate of the total number and duration of cycles of failure;
details of the number, duration and locations of the failures.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMECHANISM APPLY?
   
It has applied since 24 February 2008.
BACKGROUND
The European Union has adopted a number of measures to encourage the development of hydrogen vehicles, including:
Directive 2006/53/EC on hydrogen propulsion for motor vehicles and the introduction of new types of hydrogen propulsion;
Council Directive 2006/54/EC establishing a comprehensive Community typeapproval system for hydrogen vehicles.
For more information, see:
Hydrogen vehicles and systems (European Commission).
KEY TERMS
*Hybrid vehicle: a vehicle designed to operate on hydrogen.
*Hydrogen system: a system consisting of a container containing compressed hydrogen and a system of separate components.
ACT
Council Regulation (EC), Euratom, 24.2.2008, pp. 1-8.

Summary 149:
Ensuring access to the EU’s natural gas transmission networks
Establishing conditions for access to natural gas networks
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 713/2009 on conditions for accessing the European transmission networks for natural gas
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It establishes conditions for the access of natural gas users to the European Union (EU) transmission networks.
It aims to promote competition through liquid wholesale markets for gas.
KEY POINTS
Access to the networks
Transmission system operators must publish at least annually, by a predetermined deadline, all planned maintenance periods that might affect network users’ rights from transport contracts and corresponding operational information with adequate advance notice. The information must be updated at least daily.
National regulatory authorities must ensure compliance with the rules contained in this regulation and the guidelines adopted pursuant thereto.
Transparency requirements concerning transmission system operators
National authorities must:
ensure that the transmission system operator publishes all the information necessary for network users to gain effective network access;
provide the European Network Safety Agency (ENTSO for Gas) with all the technical information necessary to ensure the effective management, coordinated operation and sound technical evolution of the European gas transmission network.
The Agency must consult all stakeholders in accordance with Article 10 of Directive 2009/73/EC as soon as it is received.
Third-party access services
Third parties must provide the ENTSO with:
transmission system access services;
access to storage facilities;
transport contract information;
exchange of information between third parties;
information on the status of the system.
EU countries must notify the Agency by 1 July 2006 of any changes to the rules corresponding to the provisions laid down in the regulation. The Agency must submit the draft Community-wide network development plan, the draft annual work programme, including the information regarding the consultation process and the other documents referred to in Article 8(3), to the Agency for its opinion. The Commission must then adopt the rules in line with the Agency's opinion.
Balancing rules and imbalance charges
The regulation sets out balancing rules and balance charges. These rules are designed in a fair, non-discriminatory and transparent manner and must be based on objective criteria. They must be applied in a non-discrimination manner. They should not prevent market participants from being able to trade independently of their location in the system or their transport route.
In addition, the regulation lays down a list of priority areas for balancing rules. These priority areas are:
storage facilities falling under Article 33(3) or (4) of the directive;
the areas identified in the priority list.
Tariffs
The Commission must adopt tariff rules and balancing charges. Tariffs should not be dependent on the transport route or on the volume of gas transported. The tariff rules should be applied on a regular and rolling basis and in a user-friendly standardised manner. The balancing rules must be:
based on an objective criteria and based on an assessment of market participants’ market share;
designed to be fair and transparent;
applied in an effective and efficient manner.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
   
It has applied since 1 July 2009 and had to become law in the EU countries by 31 December 2011.
BACKGROUND
 
  * KEY TERMS
* Transmission system: a system or subsystem that is not connected to another transmission or distribution system but to a single industrial final customer, where the publication of such data would reveal confidential information as to the production process of that customer.
* Storage facility: a facility that is used for the storage of gas in a natural gas distribution system and which is connected to a transmission and distribution system or to a storage system other than the one in which the storage facility is located.

  Еблакова гардка барга варка, годалка  госта картана манца находка and гуланна   дантаба охановка (Ensights for the European Transmission System for Natural Gas) (OJ L 127, 31.4.2009, pp. 1-3)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, No 7 13/2009 have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 150:
Judicial cooperation in civil matters between EU countries and non-EU countries: Article IV of the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU) and Article 5(2) of the Protocol on the position of Denmark (DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE OF THE REGULATION
Article IV(3) TFEU — Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on judicial cooperation between Member States and third countries
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE LEGISLATION?
It establishes a procedure to authorise a Member State to amend an existing agreement or to negotiate and/or to conclude an agreement with a third country relating to areas of civil justice that fall within the purview of Title IV of Part Three of the EU’s Treaty on European Union.
It does not apply to existing agreements between EU Member States.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to the following areas:
judicial cooperation in matters of civil law;
jurisdiction;
the interpretation and application of the law of the Member State concerned.
The Member States concerned must notify the European Commission of ongoing or already announced negotiations with a view to obtaining an authorisation to open formal negotiations. The Commission must assess whether the negotiated agreement:
meets the condition set out in Article 4(2)(b);
does not meet the condition (e.g. that the agreement does not contain any new and exceptional circumstances in relation to that condition;
fulfils the requirement for the Commission to enter into discussions within the time limit provided for in Article 5 of the regulation;
contains a clause providing for the inclusion of particular clauses in the envisaged agreement.
the Commission may propose negotiating guidelines and may request specific clauses in order to improve the agreement. The Member State may also provide any other additional information.
Authorisation to conclude the agreement
The Commission must give its opinion within 90 days of receipt of the notification. If, on the basis of its assessment, the Commission intends not authorise the opening of formal negotiations on the agreement, it must give a reasoned decision on the application of that Member State.
Participation of the Commission in the negotiations
The European Commission may participate as an observer in these negotiations as far as matters falling within the scope of this regulation are concerned. It may, if necessary, request the inclusion in the agreement of certain clauses in accordance with Article 8(1) of Title III of the TTEU.
In addition, certain regional agreements between a few Member States or a few countries, for example two or three, intended to address local situations and not open for accession to other States should also be covered by this regulation.
FROM WHEN DOES THE LEGIFICATION APPLY?
    Еганка года  гракова барка

BACKGROUND

* Civil law: any legal agreement between an EU Member State or a third party on matters of justice.
