Summary 175:
Convention on the rational conservation and management of fishery resources in the Area defined by the Convention on the Conservation and Management of Fishery Resources in the Convention Area (the Convention Area).
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1224/2009 on the convention of the International Committee of the Red Sea — Convention on rational conservation, management and sustainable use of fisheries
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
It aims to ensure that the convention’s rules are implemented.
The convention provides for an appropriate framework for multilateral cooperation on the conservation and managed fishery resource in the area defined by it.
KEY POINTS
The regulation applies to:
fishing vessels flying the flag of a non-contracting party;
fishery resources frozen after being caught in the convention area;
non-governmental organisations (NGOs) that are involved in IUU activities.
EU countries must:
ensure that vessels flying their flag which fish or plan to fish in the regulation area are inspected before they enter their ports;
monitor the vessel monitoring system (VMS) and the identification of vessels that might be carrying out illicit fishing activities;
identify vessels that are carrying out illegal fishing activities and inform the European Commission and the International Maritime Organization (IMO) of any such vessels.
National authorities must ensure that all vessels entering one of their ports are inspected.
Vessel monitoring system
Member States must ensure the automatic and electronic transmission to the NEAFC Secretary of information obtained by the VMS, including:
the name and registration number of the vessel;
the total round weight by species which are to be off-loaded or which have been on-loaded in kilograms and the call signs of the donor and receiving vessels. The Commission must forward the information promptly to the Secretary.
Monitoring and identifying of vessels
The VMS must be used to identify vessels that may be involved in illegal fishing. Member States must also designate and notify the IMO of ports where the landing or transhipment of illicit fishery products frozen after falling into the convention Area by fishing vessels of another contracting party are permitted.
Implementing measures
The European Union (EU) has adopted implementing measures. These include:
implementing rules for the monitoring of vessels flying its flag;
rules for the identification and tracking of vessels which are suspected of carrying out IUU fishing activities. These rules apply to vessels flying either the flag or the registration of a vessel.
Inspections and follow-up
The Commission must carry out inspections on board any fishing vessel without prior notice being transmitted by radio to that vessel or without that vessel being given the appropriate signal using the International Code of Signals, including the identity of the inspection platform. The inspection must be carried out under the authority of the flag EU country. If the vessel is found to be in breach of the rules, the vessel must be towed to a port designated by that EU country for a thorough inspection under its authority. The reasons for exceeding the limit laid down in paragraph 6 shall be recorded in the inspection report referred to in paragraph 9.
If serious infringements are found, the Commission may require the fishing vessel to proceed immediately, and in any case within 24 hours, to a designated port. The vessel must then be handed over to the competent authority for a further inspection.
Reports
Member countries must report to the Commission any information which might be relevant to the identification or tracking of IUU vessels. They must also submit to the body designated by it any further information which could be relevant for the verification of the conservation or management measures adopted by the convention. In addition to surveillance reports and information on inspections, Member States may at any time submit reports on any non-compliance with the convention or the rules.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?

It has applied since 1 January 2010.
BACKGROUND
The Convention on Fisheries and Aquaculture (Convention Area) is a multilateral agreement which aims to conserve and manage fisheries in accordance with the principles set out in Article 1(2) of the Convention.
For more information, see:
Fishery Resources (European Commission).
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EC, Euratom) No 621/2009 of 21 December 2009 on the Convention of the Indian Red Sea – Convention on Rational Conservation, Management and Sustainable Use of Fisheries in the Agreement on the Regulation of the European Red Sea (OJ L 157, 23.12.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (Euratom) no 621 have been incorporated into the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Summary 176:
EU Ecolabel — environmental label
EU EColabel — environmentally friendly products
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 552/2009 on the European Union Ecolabelling scheme
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
   
It establishes a European Union (EU) ecolabel* to help consumers better understand the environmental impact of products and services.
It sets out the criteria for assessing the compliance of products with the EU Eligible Products Directive (Ecodesign).
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to any goods or services which are supplied for distribution, consumption or use on the EU market whether in return for payment or free of charge (hereinafter ‘products’).
It does not apply to energy-related products.
The European Commission is responsible for establishing the criteria and assessing the products’ compliance with the Ecodesign requirements. These criteria are based on the most significant environmental impacts of products during their whole life cycle. The criteria are set out in the regulation’s Annex I.
Requirements
The Commission must:
establish requirements for assessing compliance of specific products;
specify, for each product group, three key environmental characteristics that may be displayed in the optional label with text box described in Annex II;
define the relevant period of validity of the criteria, the assessment requirements, and the degree of product variability allowed during the period during which the criteria are valid;
assess the environmental characteristics of the products during the assessment period.
apply the criteria to all goods and services supplied on the market.
Review and revision of the European Eligibility List
The Eligibilities List of products covered by the regulation are:
products that meet the criteria;
products which do not comply with the criteria.
In addition, the Commission may adopt the criteria on the basis of scientific evidence and other scientific evidence that it considers to be relevant to the objectives of the regulation.
Market surveillance and control of the use of the EU eligible products
The Regulation establishes a market surveillance body to monitor and control the use and use of EU Elegible Products. The body must receive all relevant documentation, as specified in the relevant Commission measure establishing criteria for the product group in question, within 6 months of receiving a notification from the Commission, and must complete the documentation within six months after receiving the notification. It must also carry out on-site inspections and verifications of products in question.
Eligibility of small and medium-sized enterprises (SMEs) and operators in developing countries
The SMEs must submit an application to the Commission for the use, in accordance with the regulation, of an optional label containing the following information:
the name of the product;
the product group;
a description of its environmental characteristics;
an environmental impact statement.
If the Commission considers that a product does not meet the requirements, it must inform the SME of the reasons for its exclusion from the list of eligible products. The SME must also provide the Commission with all the relevant information on the product, including:
its environmental impact;
how the product complies with the requirements;
whether the product is likely to be hazardous to human health, the environment or the economy;
if the product has been manufactured in a non-EU country, whether the product meets the criteria or not.
FROM WHEN DOES THE RECOMMENDATION APPLY?
It has applied since 26 October 2009 and had to become law in the EU countries by 26 October 2011.
BACKGROUND
 
The ecodesign scheme was established in 2000 and has been amended several times, most recently in 2009.
For more information, see:
‘Ecolabel’ (European Commission).
* KEY TERMS
* Ecodesign: an environmental label designed to inform consumers of the environmental benefits of a product or service.
* Environmental impact statement: a statement describing the environmental impacts that products have as a result of their use.
MAIN DOCUMENT
  i.e. a description of the major environmental impact that products or services have on the environment.
Council Regulation (EC, No 550/2009) of 27 October 2009 on the introduction of an EU Eco-Label (OJ L 127, 28.10.2009, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EEC, no 550/09) have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.

Summary 177:
Protection of medicinal products protected by patents
Protection against patent fraud
SUMMARY OF:
Regulation (EC) No 1901/2006 on the protection of medicines protected by a patent
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE REGULATION?
  
It codifies and repeals Regulation (EEC, No 1768/92, which had to become law in the European Union (EU) countries by 2 January 1993.
It aims to ensure that the protection conferred by patents on medicinal products does not undermine the free movement of these products within the EU.
KEY POINTS
Scope
The regulation applies to:
any medicinal product protected by patent and for which the first authorisation to place it on the market as a medicinal product was obtained after 1 January 2000, provided that the application for a certificate was lodged within 6 months from 1 May 2004;
any patent protected by an invention which has been extended or for which such extension was applied for, under national law.
The term of protection granted under a patent is reduced by the number of years by which the term of the patent exceeds 20 years.
Subject matter of protection
Within the limits of patent protection, the protection granted by a certificate shall extend only to the product covered by the authorisation and the product identified in that authorisation.
Duration of the certificate
The certificate may be renewed for a period of up to 20 years, or for a maximum of 30 years. The duration may be extended by 6 months in the case where Article 36 of the regulation applies.
An application for an extension of the duration of a certificate must contain the following information:
the name and address of the holder
the number of the basic patent
the title of the invention
the authorisation
the date and authorisation of placing the product on the European market
the duration of the protection
the product identified.
If the certificate is granted, the holder must notify the competent national authority of the EU country in which the application was lodged. The notification must contain at least the following details:
name and address
the patent
name of the authorising authority and the number and date of the initial authorisation for the placing on the EU market of the product;
the amount of the annual fees to be paid by the holder.
FROM WHEN DOES THE REGULE APPLY?
It has applied since 1 May 2006.
BACKGROUND
The European Medicines Agency (EMSA) is responsible for the regulation’s implementation.
For more information, see:
‘Protected medicinal products’ on the EMSA website.
* KEY TERMS
* Patent: a patent granted by an inventor on the basis of an invention.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Regulation (EU, Euratom) No 1011/2006 of 20 April 2006 on the regulation conferring protection of a patent on medicines protected with a basic patent (codified version) (OJ L 12, 1.5.2006, pp. 1-8)
Successive amendments to Regulation (EC, EEC, L 12) have been incorporated in the original text. This consolidated version is of documentary value only.
RELATED DOCUMENTS
 
Regulations (EC), Euratom and Euratom of the European Parliament and of the Council of 11 December 2004 on the establishment of a system for the exchange of information on patents and on the recognition of patents, amending Regulations (EC).
See consolidated version.
Communication from the European Commission to the Council, the European Economic and Social Committee and the Committee of the Regions on the implementation of the Regulation conferring patent protection on medicines (COM(2006) 652 final of 21.12.2006)
last update 04.02.2016



Summary 178:
Convention on jurisdiction in civil and commercial matters — Lugano Convention (2005 Convention on jurisdiction) (European Convention on the jurisdiction of courts and tribunals) (OJ C 202, 29.10.2005)
Convention upon jurisdiction in Civil and Commercial Matters — Lugan Convention (Oj C 202) (EEC Convention)
SUMMARY OF:
Decision 2005/852/EC on the conclusion of the Convention on Jurisdiction in Civil And Commercial Matters
Conventions on jurisdiction
WHAT IS THE AIM OF THE DECISION AND THE CONVENTION?
The decision concludes the Convention concerning jurisdiction in matters arising from the Treaty on the Functioning of the European Union (TFEU).
The convention aims to ensure that the courts of the EU countries that are party to the convention have exclusive jurisdiction in all matters relating to the registration or validity of any European patent granted for that EU country irrespective of whether the issue is raised by way of an action or as a defence.
KEY POINTS
Jurisdiction
Each EU country has exclusive jurisdiction, regardless of its domicile, in proceedings concerning:
the registration, validity or application for a European patent;
the application for an EU patent, irrespective of its validity;
any action brought against a settlor, trustee or beneficiary, if relations between these persons or their rights or obligations under the trust are involved.
The courts of each EU country must apply the law of the court or tribunal of the country in which the action is brought.
Where a judgment is brought, the court of that country is responsible for the enforcement of the judgment. The court must apply its law in the place where the harmful event occurred or may occur. The judgment may not be recognised if it conflicts with Sections 3, 4 or 6 of Title II, or in a case provided for in Article 68.
A judgment may be declared enforceable only where the party against whom enforcement is sought is not domiciled in any of the countries bound by this convention.
In addition, the parties may request a declaration of enforceability limited to parts of a judgment. This declaration must be accompanied by a translation into English and French.
DATE OF ENTRY INTO FORCE
  
The Convention entered into force on 19 October 2005.
BACKGROUND
The treaty is one of a series of international agreements on jurisdiction which aim to improve the protection of the rights and obligations of citizens of EU countries.
For more information, see:
‘The Treaty on European Union’ on the European Commission’s website.
MAIN DOCUMENT
Council Decision 2005/884/EC of 29 October 2005 concerning the conclusion, on behalf of the United Kingdom and Ireland, and of the Protocols and Annexes to the Convention of Lugano on jurisdiction concerning the registration and validity of patents granted for the European Patent Office (EFCO Convention) and on the application of Article II of Protocol 1.
Council Conventions on the Jurisdictional Limitations of Courts and Tribunals (EC) No 44/2001 and the Convention relating to COUNCIL REGULATION (EU) No 852/2001, and amending Protocols I, II and III of Protocols III and IV of Protocol I.
RELATED DOCUMENTS

Communications from the European External Action Service (EEAS) to the Council and the European Atomic Energy Community (EEAC) on the implementation by the EU of the Rome Protocol on the legal bases for the application by the Member States of the Treaty of Rome on the Law of the Court of Justice of the Union on the interpretation and application of Articles 79 and 80 of Protocol 2 to Article 80 of the Council of Justice on the Rules of Procedure of the International Court of Auditors as regards the interpretation, application and interpretation of Article 79 and 84 of the Treaties on the Interpretation and Interpretation of Articles 81 and 82 of the TECO Conventions.
